Permissibility of Making an Umm Walad a Mukatabah
Ruling on making an umm walad a mukatab, with objections and responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making an umm walad a mukatab and explain the proof based on the compatibility of kitabah and istilad and the qiyas from qisas.

Core Idea
Making an umm walad a mukatab is valid: she needs freedom before death, and kitabah and istilad are compatible concurrent paths.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the permissibility of a master making his umm walad (slave mother of his child) a mukatab. It explains the ruling in detail, including the consequences if the master dies before payment or if she pays before his death. The text also answers two objections: one regarding an apparent contradiction between kitabah and istilad, and another based on qiyas arguing that since the umm walad is not mutaqawwam, she cannot be exchanged for a ransom. We will analyze each part step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
State the ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) for a master to make his umm walad a mukatab. Note the two avenues to freedom: kitabah (by payment) and istilad (at master's death).
The passage opens with 'jaza' (it is permissible).
2
Understand Compatibility of Kitabah and Istilad
Explain why there is no contradiction: each avenue operates independently; one does not negate the other. The umm walad has 'two avenues' (jihataan) to freedom.
Objection 1 claims contradiction; response says they are concurrent.
3
Analyse the Two Scenarios
Trace what happens if the master dies before payment (freedom by istilad, ransom drops, kitabah becomes invalid but earnings/children given) and if she pays before death (freedom by kitabah).
If master dies, the contract's purpose fails; if paid, it succeeds.
4
Examine the Qiyas Objection
Understand the objection: since umm walad is not mutaqawwam (valuable property) according to Abu Hanifa, how can a valuable ransom be taken in exchange?
The objection is based on analogy from sale.
5
Apply the Qiyas Response
Study the Hanafi response: milk al-raqabah (ownership of the substance) is what is exchanged, not the property's mutaqawwam nature. The analogy from qisas (right to retaliation) shows that ownership itself can be a subject of exchange.
This is the qiyas panel: asl = qisas, far' = kitabah of umm walad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آقا نے ام ولد کو مکاتب بنا دیا تو جائز ہے
قال و اذا كاتب المولى ام ولده جاز لحاجتها الى استفادة الحرية قبل موت المولى وذلك بالكتابة ولا تنافى بينهما لأنه تلقتها جهنا حرية فان مات المولى عتقت بالاستيلاد لتعلق عتقها بموت السيد وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة لأن الغرض من ايجاب البدل العتق عند الاداء فاذا عتقت قبله لا يمكن توفير الغرض عليه فسقط وبطلت الكتابة لامتناع ابقائها من غير فائدة غير انه تسلم لها الاكساب والاولاد لان الكتابة انفسخت في حق البدل وبقيت فى حق الاولاد والاكساب لان الفسخ لنظرها والنظر فيما ذكرنا ولو ادت المكاتبة قبل موت المولى عتقت بالكتابة لانها باقية
ترجمہ اگر آقا نے اپنی ام ولد کو مکاتب کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو آقا کی موت سے پہلے آزادی حاصل کرنے کی احتیاج ہے اور یہ کتابت ہی سے حاصل ہوگی۔ اور ان دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس کو حریت کی دو جہتیں حاصل ہیں۔ پھر اگر آقا مر گیا تو ام ولد ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ آقا کی موت کے ساتھ اس کی آزادی متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اس سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بدل واجب کرنے سے غرض آزادی تھی ادا ئیگی کے وقت اور جب وہ اس سے پہلے ہی آزاد ہو گئی تو تو فیر غرض ممکن نہیں رہی لہذا مال ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور کتابت باطل ہو گئی۔ اس کو بے فائدہ باقی رکھنے کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ سے ۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ اس کو اس کی کمائی اور اولاد سپرد کر دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ کتابت بدل کے حق میں نسخ ہوگئی اور اولاد و کمائی کے حق میں باقی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ نسخ کتابت اس کی بہتری کے لئے ہے اور بہتری اسی میں ہے جو ہم نے بیان کیا اور اگر مکاتبہ نے آقا کی موت سے پہلے مال ادا کر دیا تو وہ بوجہ کتابت آزاد ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ ابھی وہ باقی ہے۔ تشریح قوله واذا كاتب المولى ... الخ ۔ اگر آقا نے اپنی ام ولد کو مکاتب کر دیا تو کتابت جائز ہے۔ اس لیے کہ ام ولد آقا کی موت کے بعد آزاد ہونے والی ہے تاہم اس سے پہلے بھی اس کو آزاد ہونے کی احتیاج ہے اور یہ بات کتابت ہی کے ذریعہ سے حاصل ہوگی ۔ پھر کتابت و استیلاد میں کوئی منافات بھی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد نے آزادی کی دو جہتیں پائی ہیں۔ لہذا کتابت صحیح ہوگی۔ سوال یہ کہنا غلط ہے کہ کتابت و استیلاد میں کوئی منافات نہیں۔ منافات تو موجود ہے اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ایک یعنی کتابت کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ آزادی بذریعہ بدل ہو اور دوم یعنی استیلاد کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ آزادی بلا بدل ہو اور ظاہر ہے کہ محق واحد ان دونوں سے ثابت نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ فكانا متنافيين
جواب منافات اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ کتابت و استیلاد عتق کی دو جہتیں ہیں جو ام ولد کو بطریق بدل حاصل ہوئی ہیں۔ سوال قیاس تو یہی چاہتا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کو مکاتب کرنا جائز نہیں ہونا چاہیے اس لئے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کی مالیت متقوم نہیں ہے تو اس کے مقابلہ میں قیمتی بدل کیسے آسکتا ہے؟ جواب آقا کے لئے اس کی ام ولد میں ملک ید اور ملک رقبہ دونوں حاصل ہوتی ہیں۔ اور عقد کتابت فی الحال ملک ید کو اٹھانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور فی المال ملک رقبہ کو اٹھانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور ملک ایسی چیز ہے جس کے مقابلہ میں قیمتی بدل آ سکتا ہے۔ گو وہ خود متقوم نہ ہو۔ جیسے ملک قصاص ہے کہ اگر بعض اولیاء معقول معاف کر دیں۔ تو باقی دوسروں کے حصہ کے مقابلہ میں مال آتا ہے۔ قوله فان مات المولى ... الخ - پھر اگر بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے پہلے آقا کا انتقال ہو جائے تو ام ولد مفت آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کی آزادی آقا کی موت سے متعلق ہو چکی تھی۔ اور اس کے ذمہ سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ ایجاب بدل کتابت کی غرض یہ تھی کہ اس کی ادائیگی کے وقت آزادی حاصل ہو اور جب آزادی اس سے پہلے ہی حاصل ہوگئی تو غرض مذکور کی تو فیر ناممکن ہوگئی۔ لہذا مال کتابت ساقط ہو گیا اور کتابت باطل ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ اس کو بے فائدہ باقی رکھنا منع ہے۔ لیکن اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ مذکورہ ام ولد کو اسکی کمائی اور اولاد سپرد کر دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ عوض کے حق میں کتابت فسخ ہوگئی اور اکساب و اولاد کے حق میں باقی ہے اس لئے کہ فسخ کتابت تو ام ولد کی بہتری کے پیش نظر ہے اور بہتری اسی میں ہے کہ ام ولد کے حق میں کتابت فسخ ہو جائے ۔ اور اکساب و اولاد کے حق میں باقی رہے۔ قوله تسلم لها الاكساب .. الخ - صاحب عنایہ نے کہا ہے کہ سلم بالا ولا حل نظر ہے۔ کیونکہ مذکور تعلیل کے پیش نظر اس کے ذکر کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔ اس لئے کہ اگر کتابت کو اولاد کے حق میں بھی فسخ مانا جائے تب بھی بہتری باقی رہتی ہے۔ کیونکہ بچہ کا حکم ماں کا حکم ہے۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں اولاد سے مراد وہ اولاد ہے جو کتابت ام سے پہلے آقا کے علاوہ کسی اور کے نطفہ سے مولود ہے اور اس کو ماں
The master made his umm walad a mukatab, so it is permissible.
He (al-Quduri) said: 'And if the master makes his umm walad a mukatab, it is permissible, because she needs to obtain freedom before the master's death, and that is through kitabah, and there is no contradiction between them because she has received two avenues of freedom. If the master dies, she becomes free through istilad because her freedom is tied to the death of the master, and the kitabah ransom falls from her, because the purpose of imposing the ransom was freedom at the time of payment; when she becomes free before that, it is not possible to fulfill that purpose upon it, so it falls and the kitabah becomes invalid due to the impossibility of keeping it without benefit. However, her earnings and children are handed over to her, because the kitabah is rescinded with respect to the ransom, but remains with respect to the children and earnings, because the rescission is for her benefit, and the benefit is as we mentioned. And if the mukatabah pays before the master's death, she becomes free through kitabah because it still exists.'
Translation: If the master makes his umm walad a mukatab, it is permissible, because she has a need to obtain freedom before the master's death, and this is only achieved through kitabah. There is no contradiction between them because she has two avenues of freedom. Then if the master dies, she becomes free due to being umm walad, because her freedom is tied to the master's death. And the kitabah ransom falls from her, because the purpose of imposing the ransom was freedom at the time of payment, and when she becomes free before that, that purpose is no longer possible, so the wealth falls and the kitabah becomes invalid due to the impossibility of keeping it without benefit. However, her earnings and children are entrusted to her, because the kitabah is rescinded with respect to the ransom and remains with respect to children and earnings, because the rescission of the kitabah is for her benefit, and the benefit is as we have explained. And if the mukatabah pays before the master's death, she becomes free by virtue of the kitabah because it still exists.
Commentary on his saying: 'And if the master makes... etc.' If the master makes his umm walad a mukatab, the kitabah is valid, because the umm walad is to become free after the master's death, but she also needs freedom before that, and this is achieved only through kitabah. There is no contradiction between kitabah and istilad because the umm walad has obtained two avenues to freedom. Therefore, the kitabah is valid.
Question: It is incorrect to say there is no contradiction between kitabah and istilad. There is a contradiction because one of them, i.e., kitabah, requires freedom through payment, and the second, i.e., istilad, requires freedom without payment, and it is clear that a single right cannot be established by both. So they are contradictory.
Answer: There is no contradiction because kitabah and istilad are two avenues to freedom that the umm walad has obtained as alternate paths.
Question: Analogy would require that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, making an umm walad a mukatab should not be permissible, because according to Imam Abu Hanifah, the umm walad is not mutaqawwam property, so how can a valuable ransom be against her?
Answer: The master has over his umm walad both milk al-yad (right of possession) and milk al-raqabah (right of ownership). The contract of kitabah immediately removes milk al-yad and eventually removes milk al-raqabah at payment. Ownership (milk) is a thing against which a valuable ransom can be given, even if the object itself is not mutaqawwam. Like the ownership of qisas: if some of the [qualified] heirs forgive [the killer], then money comes in exchange for the shares of the others.
His saying: 'If the master dies... etc.' Then if the master dies before payment of the kitabah ransom, the umm walad becomes free for free, because her freedom had already been tied to the master's death. And the kitabah ransom falls from her liability, because the purpose of imposing the kitabah ransom was that freedom would be obtained at the time of its payment; when freedom is obtained before that, that purpose becomes impossible. Therefore, the kitabah wealth falls and the kitabah becomes invalid, because keeping it without benefit is prohibited. However, it is necessary that the mentioned umm walad be entrusted with her earnings and children, because the kitabah is rescinded with respect to the consideration and remains with respect to earnings and children, because the rescission of the kitabah is for the benefit of the umm walad, and the benefit is that the kitabah is rescinded in her favor and remains in the right of earnings and children.
His saying: 'Her earnings are handed over... etc.' The author of al-‘Inayah said that the phrase 'her earnings are handed over to her and her children' is [superfluous]? Because based on the mentioned reasoning, there is no need for its mention, since even if the kitabah is considered rescinded with respect to children too, the benefit remains, because the child's ruling follows the mother's ruling.
The answer is that 'children' here refers to those children who were born before the kitabah from a sperm other than the master's, and they are [attached] to the mother.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of a master making his umm walad (slave mother of his child) a mukatab. It is valid because she needs freedom before the master's death, and kitabah provides that avenue. There is no contradiction between kitabah and istilad because they are two independent routes to freedom. If the master dies, she becomes free by istilad, and the kitabah ransom drops. If she pays before his death, she becomes free by kitabah. The commentary then addresses two objections: (1) an apparent contradiction between kitabah and istilad (paid vs. free) – resolved by noting they are concurrent paths; (2) a qiyas objection based on Abu Hanifa's view that umm walad is not mutaqawwam property – answered by distinguishing between milk al-raqabah and milk al-yad, and citing the analogy of qisas. Finally, a critical note from Sahib al-‘Inayah is addressed regarding the phrase 'her earnings and children are given to her,' explaining that 'children' here refers to those born before the kitabah from another father.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to a child from her master, thereby acquiring the status that she becomes free upon the master's death.
استیلاد (istilad): The legal status of being an umm walad, which results in automatic freedom upon the master's death.
ملک ید (milk al-yad): The right of possession or usufruct, as opposed to full ownership (milk al-raqabah). In this context, the master has both over the umm walad.
ملک رقبہ (milk al-raqabah): The right of full ownership over the substance of a property, including the right to transfer ownership.
کتابت (kitabah): A contract in which a slave agrees to pay a ransom to the master in exchange for freedom.
مکاتب (mukatab): A male slave who is under a kitabah contract; the feminine is mukatabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if a master makes his umm walad a mukatab and she pays the full ransom before his death, what is her status?
A) She becomes free by istilad only, not by kitabah.
B) She becomes free by kitabah because the contract is still in effect.
C) She remains a slave until the master dies.
D) She becomes free but must pay an additional compensation to the master's heirs.

Key Takeaway
Making an umm walad a mukatab is permissible because kitabah and istilad are compatible avenues to freedom, and the contract is valid because it exchanges ownership (milk) for a ransom, not the property's value.

intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Making Umm Walad a Mukatab and Effect of Master's Death
Explains the ruling on umm walad's kitabah and its effect when master dies before payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of kitabah for an umm walad, explain the objection based on non-mutaqawwim and the qiyas response, and determine the consequences when the master dies before payment.

Core Idea
Kitabah for an umm walad is valid because the payment is for the right of ownership, not for her person, analogous to qisas.

The umm walad occupies a unique position in Hanafi law: she is not a commodity during the master's life, yet she can be made a mukatab. This raises a crucial question — if she is not mutaqawwim, how can a price be taken for her freedom? The commentator resolves this by shifting the focus from her person to the master's right of ownership (milk al-raqabah), drawing a powerful analogy to qisas. We will then examine what happens when the master dies before the kitabah payment: a change in status that triggers a cascade of legal effects on her earnings and children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its immediate justification
Locate the statement that the kitabah of umm walad is jā'iz (valid). Note the reason given: the umm walad needs freedom both after the master's death and before it, and kitabah provides a path to pre-death freedom. Recognise that kitabah and istilad are not contradictory—they represent two aspects of her right to freedom.
The commentator explicitly states 'la munāfāt bayna al-kitābah wa al-istīlād' (no contradiction).
2
Analyse the objection and the qiyas response
The objector argues that since Imam Abu Hanifa holds the umm walad is not mutaqawwim, no monetary payment can be validly taken for her. Trace the Hanafi response: the master has both milk al-yad (possession) and milk al-raqabah (corpus ownership). The kitabah contract removes milk al-yad immediately and eventually milk al-raqabah. Payment is for the right of ownership, not for the person. Draw the analogy to qisas: when some heirs forgive their share of retaliation, the remaining heirs may take money in lieu. Just as money can be taken for the right of qisas even though the act of retaliation itself is not a commodity, so too can payment be taken for the right of ownership of the umm walad.
This is a classic jaliyy qiyas: the illa is that payment is for a right (haqq), not the physical entity.
3
Examine the effect of the master's death before payment
The passage then shifts to a scenario: the master dies before the umm walad pays the kitabah money. Identify the ruling: she becomes free automatically due to istilad, and the kitabah payment is dropped. Understand the reasoning: the purpose of the payment was to attain freedom at the time of payment; since freedom has already occurred (through death), the purpose is impossible, so the payment is voided and the kitabah becomes bāṭil (void).
The kitabah is not simply cancelled; it becomes bāṭil because keeping it without benefit is prohibited.
4
Apply the nuance of earnings and children
Despite the kitabah being voided, the passage states that her earnings and children (born from another man) are given to her. This is because the dissolution (fasakh) of kitabah is only with respect to the badal (substitute); it remains effective regarding earnings and children, for her benefit. This is an exception based on the principle that the dissolution is for her betterment (iṣlāḥ).
The commentary clarifies that 'children' here excludes the master's own children from the umm walad; they follow the mother's status and are free upon master's death anyway.

Her earnings and children will be given to her. Because the kitabah is abrogated with respect to the substitute (badal), but it remains with respect to children and earnings. Because the abrogation of kitabah is for her betterment, and betterment lies in what we have stated. If the female mukatab pays the money before the master's death, she becomes free due to kitabah, because it is still valid. Explanation of his statement: 'And when the master makes his umm walad a mukatab...' etc. If the master makes his umm walad a mukatab, the kitabah is valid. Because the umm walad is to become free after the master's death, but she also needs freedom before that, and this is obtained through kitabah. There is no contradiction between kitabah and istilad. Because the umm walad has two aspects of freedom. Therefore the kitabah is valid. Objection: The statement that there is no contradiction between kitabah and istilad is wrong. There is contradiction because one (kitabah) requires freedom through payment, and the other (istilad) requires freedom without payment, and a single right cannot be established by both. So they are contradictory. Answer: The contradiction is not present because kitabah and istilad are two aspects of the right (haqq) that the umm walad obtains through payment. Objection: Analogy demands that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, making umm walad a mukatab should not be permissible, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the umm walad is not a property of value (mutaqawwim), so how can a payment of value be given in exchange? Answer: The master has both ownership of possession (milk al-yad) and ownership of the corpus (milk al-raqabah) in his umm walad. The contract of kitabah removes the ownership of possession immediately, and eventually removes the ownership of the corpus. Ownership is a thing for which a payment of value can be given, even if the owned object itself is not of value. Like the ownership of qisas: if some of the legal heirs forgive, then money is given in exchange for the share of the others. His statement: 'If the master dies...' etc. Then if the master dies before the payment of kitabah money, the umm walad becomes free without payment. Because her freedom had become attached to the master's death. The kitabah payment is dropped from her liability. Because the purpose of imposing the kitabah payment was that she would attain freedom at the time of payment, and when freedom occurred before that, the mentioned purpose became impossible to achieve. Therefore the kitabah money is dropped, and the kitabah becomes void, because keeping it without benefit is prohibited. But it is necessary that the mentioned umm walad's earnings and children are given to her. Because the kitabah is rescinded with respect to the substitute, but remains regarding earnings and children. Because the dissolution of kitabah is for the betterment of the umm walad, and betterment lies in the kitabah being rescinded for her right and remaining for earnings and children. His statement: 'Earnings are given to her...' etc. The author of 'Inayah said that this is not necessary. Because in view of the mentioned reasoning, there is no need to mention it. Because if the kitabah is considered rescinded regarding children as well, the betterment still remains, because the child's ruling follows the mother's. The answer is that here the children meant are those who were born before the mother's kitabah from a sperm of someone other than the master, and the mother bought them during the state of kitabah. As Taj al-Shari'ah clarified. The children born from the master's sperm are not intended.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with the ruling on making an umm walad (a slave woman who has borne a child to her master) a mukatab (a slave who enters a contract of kitabah for freedom). The passage is an expansion_probe: the commentator explains the matn and addresses objections. The main ruling is that it is valid (jā'iz) for a master to make his umm walad a mukatab, despite the apparent contradiction between kitabah (which requires payment for freedom) and istilad (which grants freedom upon the master's death without payment). The commentator resolves this by stating that the umm walad has two 'aspects' to freedom: one immediate via kitabah and one deferred via istilad. An objection is raised based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view that the umm walad is not a commodity (ghayr mutaqawwim), so payment cannot be validly taken. The answer explains that the master owns both the usufruct (milk al-yad) and the corpus (milk al-raqabah), and the payment is for the right of ownership, not for the person directly, drawing an analogy to qisas where payment can be taken for a right. The passage then covers the scenario of the master's death before payment: the umm walad becomes free without paying, and the kitabah payment is voided. However, her earnings and children are given to her, because the kitabah is considered rescinded only regarding the substitute (badal) but remains regarding the earnings and children, for her benefit. A further point clarifies that the children meant here are those born from another man, not the master's own children.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to a child recognized as the master's offspring
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of kitabah with the master, agreeing to pay a sum for freedom
استیلاد (istilad): The act of a master begetting a child from his female slave, making her an umm walad
بدل (badal): The substitute or payment in the kitabah contract that the slave must provide for freedom
ملک ید (milk al-yad): Ownership of possession or usufruct
ملک رقبہ (milk al-raqabah): Ownership of the corpus or substance of the property
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Property that has legal value and can be sold or used in exchange

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master makes his umm walad a mukatab, and then the master dies before she pays the kitabah money, what happens?
A) She remains a slave and must pay the kitabah to the master's heirs
B) She becomes free without paying, but her earnings and children go to the master's estate
C) She becomes free without paying, and her earnings and children are given to her
D) The kitabah is automatically extended to the heirs

Key Takeaway
The kitabah of an umm walad is valid because the payment is for the right of ownership (milk al-raqabah), not for her person; upon the master's death before payment, she becomes free automatically and the payment is voided, but her earnings and children (from another man) are given to her for her benefit.

Mudabbara as Mukatab: Options and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mudabbara's payment options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the mudabbara's payment options and explain how the dispute stems from the principle of tajzi' al-'itq (divisibility of manumission).

Core Idea
A mudabbara has only entitlement to freedom, not actual freedom, so making her a mukatab is valid, and she may choose between two routes to freedom.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a master makes his mudabbara (a slave promised freedom after his death) a mukatab (a slave who contracts to pay for freedom). The core legal question is what happens when the master dies leaving no other property. The passage lays out an intra-Hanafi dispute among the three founding imams regarding the mudabbara's obligations and choices, rooted in the principle of whether manumission is divisible (tajzi' al-'itq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its validity
First, note that making a mudabbara a mukatab is valid (jā'iz). The commentator explains that there is no contradiction because the mudabbara does not have actual freedom, only entitlement (istihqāq).
2
Understand the master's death scenario
The master dies leaving only this mudabbara as his asset. She must now 'sa'ā' (earn or pay) to secure full freedom. The question is: what must she pay, and does she have a choice?
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that she has a choice between paying two-thirds of her value (to complete freedom via tadbir) or the full kitabah payment (to complete freedom via kitabah). The basis: manumission is divisible (tajazzu' al-'itq). One-third of her is already freed by tadbir, leaving two-thirds owned. She has two routes to freedom for that two-thirds, so she can choose.
Two routes: immediate (via tadbir) and deferred (via kitabah).
4
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa on the amount options (two-thirds value or full kitabah) but denies choice. He says she must pay the lesser of the two amounts.
No choice; the minimum is automatically applied.
5
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad also denies choice but further restricts the amounts. She must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment.
Both amount and choice are narrowed.
6
Identify the usul basis of the dispute
The commentator explains that the disagreement on choice is a branch (far') of whether manumission is divisible. Abu Hanifa accepts tajzi' al-'itq, so he gives choice. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not accept divisibility (or interpret it differently), so they deny choice. This also explains the different amount calculations.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the practical difference in payment obligations.

He said: And if he makes his mudabbara a mukatab, it is valid, due to the necessity we mentioned, and there is no contradiction, because freedom is not established; rather only entitlement is established. If the master dies and he has no property other than her, she has the choice between paying in two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah payment. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf says: She pays the lesser of the two. Muhammad says: She pays the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. So the dispute is regarding the choice and the amount. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa on the amount and with Muhammad on the negation of choice. As for choice, it is a branch of the divisibility of manumission (tajzi' al-'itq). According to him (Abu Hanifa), since manumission is divisible, two-thirds remain slave property. And she has two aspects of freedom with two payments: an immediate one through tadbir and a deferred one through kitabah, so she chooses. Translation: If he makes his mudabbara a mukatab, it is valid, due to the necessity we mentioned, and there is no contradiction, because freedom is not established; rather only entitlement is established. If the master dies and he has no property other than her, she has the choice: either to pay in two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah payment. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Abu Yusuf says: She pays the lesser of the two. Imam Muhammad says: She pays the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. So the dispute is regarding the choice and the amount. So Imam Abu Yusuf agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa on the amount and with Imam Muhammad on the negation of choice. In any case, choice is a branch of the divisibility of manumission. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since manumission is divisible, two-thirds of the corpus remain owned. And she has two aspects of freedom from two payments: one immediate through tadbir and one deferred through kitabah, so she will be entitled to choose. Explanation of his statement: 'And if he makes...' etc. If the master makes his mudabbara female slave a mukatab, this is also valid, because the mentioned need is also realized here. There is no contradiction between kitabah and tadbir, because being a mudabbara does not give her actual freedom, but merely entitlement to freedom. Now if the master dies and he has no property other than this mudabbara, then this female mukatab mudabbara will have a choice: either she pays in two-thirds of the value of her being a mudabbara, or the full kitabah payment. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Imam Yusuf, she pays whichever is lesser. According to Imam Muhammad, she pays whichever is lesser of two-thirds of the value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. Now there is disagreement here on two matters: first, whether she has a choice or not; second, what is the amount in which she will pay? So Imam Abu Yusuf agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa on the amount and with Imam Muhammad on negation of choice. The disagreement on choice and no-choice is based on whether manumission is divisible or not. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, manumission is divisible. The mentioned mudabbara has become entitled to one-third freedom (because it is known that a mudabbir, according to most scholars, becomes free from one-third, except Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and Dawud al-Zahiri). So two-thirds of her corpus remains owned. On the other hand, she has two aspects of freedom: immediate through tadbir and deferred through kitabah. Therefore she has a choice between two-thirds of her value and the full kitabah payment, whichever she wishes to pay.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an expansion_probe covering a matn from Al-Hidayah on the issue of making a mudabbara (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) a mukatab (one who contracts to buy freedom). The commentator explains that it is valid, citing the same need as for umm walad, and there is no contradiction because the mudabbara has only an entitlement to freedom (istihqāq), not actual freedom. The main part deals with the scenario of the master's death without other assets, where she must 'sa'ā' (earn or pay) to secure freedom. The passage lays out an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa gives her a choice between paying two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah amount; Abu Yusuf says she pays the lesser of those two; Muhammad says she pays the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. The commentator explains that the difference is rooted in two issues: (1) whether she has choice (ikhtiyār) and (2) the amount. Abu Yusuf aligns with Abu Hanifa on amount (two-thirds vs full) but with Muhammad on denying choice (no choice; she must pay the lesser). The basis of Abu Hanifa's view is that manumission is divisible (tajazzu’ al-'itq), so one-third of her is already freed by tadbir (since a mudabbir usually is freed from one-third of his estate upon death), leaving two-thirds owned. She has two routes to freedom for that two-thirds: immediate via tadbir (but postponed) and via kitabah (deferred). So she may choose to pay either two-thirds of her value (to complete freedom via tadbir) or the full kitabah payment (to complete freedom via kitabah). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept different premises.

Key Terms
مدبرہ (mudabbara): A female slave who has been promised freedom upon her master's death by way of tadbir (a declaration that she will be free after his death)
سعایت (sa'āyah): The act of a slave or mudabbara earning money or performing work to pay off a debt or purchase freedom
تجزئة الاعتاق (tajzi' al-i'tq): The principle that manumission can be partial; i.e., freeing a portion of a slave is valid and effects partial freedom
استحقاق (istihqāq): Entitlement or right to something, here specifically entitlement to freedom (as opposed to actual freedom)
تدبیر (tadbir): A contract or declaration by which a master promises that a slave will be free after his death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, what must the female mukatab mudabbara pay when the master dies without other property?
A) She must pay two-thirds of her value
B) She must pay the full kitabah amount
C) She must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah amount
D) She must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value or two-thirds of the kitabah amount

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the mudabbara's options after master's death illustrates how a single fiqh issue can branch into multiple valid positions based on differing usul principles, with the divisibility of manumission being the key determinant.

Mukatab Making a Mudabbara: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Options and Amount
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a mudabbara made into a mukataba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the option and amount owed when a mudabbara is made a mukataba and the master dies insolvent, and explain the underlying principle of divisibility of emancipation.

Core Idea
When one-third of a slave is already entitled to freedom, the kitabah payment is only for the remaining two-thirds, but whether she can choose between two payments depends on whether emancipation is divisible.

The Hanafi school discusses a nuanced case where a master declares his female slave as a mudabbara (free upon his death) and subsequently enters into a kitabah contract with her. If the master dies with no property except her, what must she pay? Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ on both the option (khiyar) and the amount. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of each imam, focusing on the crucial principle of divisibility of emancipation (tajazzu' al-i'taq) and its effect on contractual obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and legal question
Identify the facts: master makes his mudabbara a mukataba, dies insolvent. The key issues: (1) Does she have a choice between two payment amounts? (2) What is the exact amount she owes?
2
Identify the principle of tajazzu' al-i'taq
Recognize that the disagreement stems from whether emancipation is divisible. Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible; the Sahibayn hold it is not. This determines whether the mudabbara becomes fully free upon the master's death or only partially.
An indivisible emancipation means that once part becomes free, the entire slave is free.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position on the option
Since emancipation is divisible, two-thirds of her remains enslaved. She has two ways to freedom: immediate (tadbir) and deferred (kitabah). She may choose which payment to make: two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah.
The option is real; she can select the easier obligation.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's position on the option
Emancipation is indivisible, so upon the master's death she becomes fully free. She owes either two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah, but she will inevitably choose the lesser. Thus, no real choice exists—only an automatic selection of the minimum.
Both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad negate the option as a meaningful legal concept.
5
Distinguish between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the amount
Abu Yusuf holds she must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and the full kitabah. Muhammad holds she must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah. Muhammad argues that the one-third entitlement drops one-third of the payment, while Abu Yusuf argues the entire kitabah is for the two-thirds that remained enslaved.
The difference hinges on whether the prior entitlement reduces the consideration proportionally or not.
6
Identify the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
Later Hanafi authorities rely on Abu Yusuf's view as the operative position for fatwa. Under Abu Yusuf, she pays the lesser of two-thirds value and full kitabah. Under Muhammad, she pays less if two-thirds of kitabah is smaller. Under Abu Hanifa, she can choose the higher or lower, potentially paying more.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is the amount she actually pays, which varies by position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان كاتب مدبرته جاز لما ذكرنا من الحاجة ولا تنافى اذ الحرية غير ثابتة وانما الثابت مجرد الاستحقاق وان مات المولى ولا مال له غيرها فهى بالخيار بين ان تسعى فى ثلثي قيمتها او جميع مال الكتابة وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابويوسف تسعى فى الاقل منهما وقال محمد تسعى في الاقل من ثلثى قيمتها وثلثى بدل الكتابة فالخلاف فى الخيار والمقدار فابويوسف مع ابي حنيفة في المقدار ومع محمد فى نفى الخيار اما الخيار ففرع تجزى الاعتاق والاعتاق عنده لما تجزّى بقى الثلثان رقيقا وقد تلقتها جهتا حرية ببدلين معجلة بالتدبير وموجلة بالكتابة فتخير وعندهما لما عتق كلها بعتق بعضها فهي حرة ووجب عليها احد المالين فتختار الاقل لا محالة فلا معنى للتخير واما المقدار فلمحمد انه قابل البدل بالكل وقد سلم لها الثلث بالتدبير فمن المحال ان يجب البدل مقابلته الا ترى انه لو سلم لها الكل بان خرجت من الثلث يسقط كل بدل الكتابة فهنا يسقط الثلث فصار كما اذا تاخر التدبير عن الكتابة ولهما ان جميع البدل مقابل بثلثى رقبتها فلا يسقط منه شيء وهذا لان لبدل وان قوبل بالكل صورة وصيغة لكنه مقيد بما ذكرنا معنى وارادة لانها استحقت حرية الثلث ظاهرا و الظاهر ان الانسان لا يلتزم المال بمقابلة ما يستحق حريته وصار هذا كما اذا طلق امرأته ثنتين ثم طلقها لاثا على الف كان جميع الالف بمقابلة الواحدة الباقية لدلالة الارادة كذا ههنا بخلاف ما اذا تقدمت لكتابة وهى المسألة التي تليه لان البدل مقابل بالكل اذ لا استحقاق عنده في شيء فافترقا
He said: If he makes his mudabbara a mukataba, it is permissible due to the need we mentioned, and there is no contradiction, because freedom is not established, only mere entitlement. And if the master dies and he has no property other than her, she has the option between working for two-thirds of her value or all of the kitabah payment. This according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: She works for the lesser of the two. Muhammad said: She works for the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. So the disagreement is in the option and the amount. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa on the amount and with Muhammad on negating the option. As for the option, it is a branch of the divisibility of emancipation. According to him (Abu Hanifa), since emancipation is divisible, two-thirds remains enslaved, and two aspects of freedom have reached her with two compensations: one immediate through tadbir and one deferred through kitabah, so she chooses. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since she becomes fully free by the freedom of a part, she is free, and one of the two payments is obligatory upon her, so she inevitably chooses the lesser; thus there is no meaning to choice. As for the amount, according to Muhammad: He (the master) made the payment in exchange for the whole, and one-third has been given to her through tadbir, so it is impossible for the payment to be obligatory in exchange for it. Do you not see that if the whole had been given to her, i.e., she came out of the one-third, all of the kitabah payment would be dropped? So here one-third drops, so it is as if tadbir came after kitabah. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): All of the payment is in exchange for two-thirds of her person, so nothing drops from it. This is because although the payment is matched with the whole in form and wording, it is restricted by what we mentioned in meaning and intention, because she has become entitled to freedom of one-third manifestly, and it is apparent that a person does not commit money in exchange for that to which freedom is entitled. And this is like if a man gives his slave-wife two divorces, then gives her three divorces for a thousand, all of the thousand is in exchange for the remaining one (divorce) due to indication of intention. Similarly here, unlike when kitabah precedes, which is the next issue, because the payment is in exchange for the whole since there is no entitlement in anything, so they differ.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (khilaf) regarding the case where a master makes his mudabbara (a slave who will be freed upon his death) into a mukataba (a slave who contracts to purchase freedom). The issue arises when the master dies leaving no property except this mudabbara-mukataba. The three imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—differ on what she must pay and whether she has a choice.

Abu Hanifa holds that she has the option (khiyar) to either work for two-thirds of her market value (since one-third is already freed by tadbir) or to work for the full kitabah payment. This is because, according to Abu Hanifa, emancipation is divisible (tajazzu' al-itaq). When the master made her a mudabbara, one-third became entitled to freedom, but she is not yet free. The remaining two-thirds is still owned. The kitabah contract covers her entire self, but since one-third is already entitled to freedom, the payment for kitabah is effectively for the remaining two-thirds. However, the contract was made for the whole, so she has a choice: either pay the value of the remaining two-thirds (i.e., two-thirds of her market value) or pay the full kitabah amount. She may choose whichever is easier.

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that she does not have a choice in the sense of selecting between two distinct options. According to them, emancipation is not divisible (la yatajazzau). When a part of a slave becomes free, the entire slave becomes free. Here, when the master died, the mudabbara's one-third freedom became actual, so she becomes entirely free. Consequently, only one payment is obligatory upon her: either the kitabah payment or the two-thirds of her value, but she must pay the lesser of the two. The option (khiyar) is meaningless because reason dictates she will choose the lesser. Thus, they negate a real choice; it is a forced choice to the minimum.

Within the Sahibayn, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on the amount when the kitabah payment and the value are not simply comparable. Abu Yusuf says she must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and the full kitabah payment. Muhammad says she must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. Muhammad's reasoning: The kitabah contract was made in exchange for her entire person, but one-third of her freedom is already secured through tadbir. Therefore, it is impossible for the entire kitabah amount to be owed in exchange for the part that is already free. Just as if she had been entirely freed from the one-third (i.e., had no tadbir), the entire kitabah would be dropped, here only two-thirds of the kitabah remains binding. So she owes the lesser of two-thirds of her value (for the remaining enslaved part) and two-thirds of the kitabah payment.

Abu Yusuf, along with Abu Hanifa on the amount, argues that the entire kitabah payment is in exchange for two-thirds of her person (the part that is not entitled to freedom). Although the contract was phrased as a total exchange, the intention and meaning restrict it to the part that is actually exchangeable. Since one-third is already entitled to freedom, the master would not have contracted to receive payment for that. So nothing drops from the kitabah; she owes the full kitabah amount, but can choose to pay two-thirds of her value instead. However, since Abu Yusuf negates choice, she must pay the lesser, which would be two-thirds of her value if that is less than the full kitabah payment, or the full kitabah if that is less.

This dispute hinges on two principles: divisibility of emancipation and the effect of prior entitlement to freedom on the kitabah contract. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position according to later Hanafi scholars is that of Abu Yusuf (the lesser of two-thirds value and full kitabah), because it reconciles the two views and is practical.

Key Terms
مدبرة (mudabbara): A female slave whose master has declared that she will be free upon his death (tadbir).
مكاتبة (mukātaba): A female slave who has entered into a kitabah contract (contract of manumission by payment).
تجزىء الاعتاق (tajazzu' al-i'tāq): The divisibility of emancipation: the belief that freeing a slave can be partial and valid, applied to tadbir.
استحقاق (istiḥqāq): Entitlement to freedom, not actual freedom. In tadbir, she is entitled to freedom upon master's death.
سعاية (su‘āyah): Working to earn money to pay the kitabah or compensation; here it means paying the required amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what options does the mudabbara-mukataba have when the master dies with no property except her?
A) She must pay two-thirds of her value only.
B) She has a choice between paying two-thirds of her value or the full kitabah payment.
C) She must pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and the full kitabah payment.
D) She must pay the full kitabah payment only.

Key Takeaway
The amount a mudabbara-mukataba owes upon master's death depends on whether emancipation is divisible; the mufta bihi position (Abu Yusuf) requires her to pay the lesser of two-thirds of her value and the full kitabah payment.

Dispute on Badal Reduction for Mudabbirah Mukatabah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on badal reduction for a mudabbirah mukatabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn regarding the reduction of kitabah badal for a mudabbirah mukatabah and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When a mudabbirah mukatabah's master dies, one-third of the badal drops according to Muhammad; Sahibayn say nothing drops.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute involving a female slave who is both a mudabbirah (promised freedom upon master's death) and a mukatabah (earning freedom by payments). When the master dies, she gains freedom for one-third of her value through tadbir. The key question is: how much of her kitabah payment (badal) remains due? Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn offer different solutions based on how they interpret the scope of the badal contract.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the factual scenario: a female slave is both mudabbirah and mukatabah. The master dies, and she is freed from one-third of her value via tadbir. The question is what happens to the kitabah badal.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and his dalil
Imam Muhammad holds that one-third of the badal drops because the badal was set against the entire slave, and one-third is already freed by tadbir. Analogy: if the whole were freed from the one-third estate, the entire badal would drop.
His reasoning is based on impossibility: the part already freed cannot be subject to payment.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that no part of the badal drops because the badal is effectively against the remaining two-thirds of her value. Although formally against the whole, intention restricts it to the portion not entitled to freedom.
They analogize with divorce: if a man gives two divorces and then a third for a sum, the sum is for the final divorce only.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Imam Muhammad, she pays two-thirds of the kitabah price or two-thirds of her value, whichever is less. Under the Sahibayn, she pays the full kitabah price but can choose between paying the kitabah price or her full value, and will naturally choose the lesser.
This difference affects her financial burden and the calculation of what she must earn.
5
Note the tarjih
The text does not specify which position is preferred. The dispute is left open, and later Hanafi works may weigh in. This lesson presents the arguments without resolution.
Both positions are considered valid within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

قابل محل ہے۔ تو وہ کل مکاتب ہو جائے گی۔ اور تدبیر کی وجہ سے اس کو ایک تہائی مل گیا۔ بایں معنی کہ اس کا یک مکث آزاد ہو چکا تو لا محالہ اس کے مقابلہ میں بدل کا ایک ٹکٹ ساقط ہوگا۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر اس کو کل رقبہ مل جاتا بایں طور کہ وہ تہائی ترکہ سے برآمد ہوتی تو کل بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جاتا۔ پس یہاں ایک تہائی بدل ساقط ہو جائے گا اور وہ اپنی قیمت کے دو ثلث سے ممتر میں سعایت کرنے گی۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے آقا پہلے اپنے غلام کو مکاتب کرے پھر مد بر کر دے اس کے بعد آقا کا انتقال ہو جائے اور اس مدبر کے علاوہ اور کوئی مال نہ ہو ۔ کہ اس صورت میں بالا تفاق تہائی بدل ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ پیش نظر مسئلہ کے بعد آگے آرہا ہے۔ قوله ولهما ان جميع .... الخ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پورا بدل کتابت اس کے دو تہائی رقبہ کے مقابلہ میں ہے تو اس میں سے کچھ ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ اس کی تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ بدل کتابت تو بظاہر مدبرہ کی کل ذات کے مقابلہ میں ہے حیث قال کا تجتک نیز صیغہ کے اعتبار سے بھی کل کے مقابل میں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ خطاب سے کل ذات کی تعبیر ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن از راہ معنی وارادہ دو ٹکٹ کے مقابلہ میں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ امر ظاہر ہے کہ وہ بوجہ تدبیر ایک تہائی کی مستحق آزادی ہو چکی۔ اور یہ بھی ظاہر ہے۔ کہ جس قدر حصہ کی آزادی کا استحقاق ہو جائے اس کے مقابلہ میں آدمی اپنے اوپر مال لازم نہیں کرتا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کوئی اپنی بیوی کو دو طلاقیں دے کر پھر اس کو ہزار پر تین طلاقیں دے دے کہ بدلالت ارادہ پورے ہزار درہم باقی ایک طلاق کے مقابلہ میں ہوتے ہیں بخلاف تقدیم کتابت والے مسئلہ کے کہ اس میں پورا عوض کل رقبہ کے مقابلہ میں ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ پہلے سے کچھ استحقاق ثابت نہیں ہے۔ قوله ان الانسان لا يلتزم .. الخ ۔ اس پر کہنے والا یہ کہ سکتا ہےکہ استحقاق حریت سے حقیقت حریت لازم نہیں آتی اور مد برہ مذکورہ کو فی الحال صرف اتفاق حاصل ہے نہ کہ حقیقت حریت۔ پس یہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ فی الحال حقیقت حریت کے استفادہ کی محتاج ہو اور اسکے مقابلہ میں وہ مال کا التزام کر لے۔ چنانچہ آقابالا جماع اپنی ام ولد و مکاتب کر سکتا ہے حالانکہ وہ حریت کل کی مستحق ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ وہ موت آقا کے وقت جمیع مال سے آزاد ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مثلث ہے۔
And according to them (Sahibayn), when she becomes entirely free by freeing part, she is free and one of the two amounts is obligatory upon her, so she necessarily chooses the lesser, thus there is no meaning to choice. As for the amount, according to Muhammad he made the badal (kitabah payment) equivalent to the whole, and one-third has been granted to her by tadbir, so it is impossible for the badal to be due in exchange for it. Do you not see that if the whole was granted to her by being taken out of the one-third, all the kitabah badal would fall due, so here one-third falls away. It becomes as if the tadbir came after the kitabah. According to them (Sahibayn), all the badal is equivalent to two-thirds of her value, so nothing falls from it. This is because although the badal is formally and verbally made equivalent to the whole, it is restricted in meaning and intention by what we mentioned, because she has apparently become entitled to freedom of one-third. It is apparent that a person does not undertake payment in exchange for what one is entitled to freedom. This is like if a man divorces his wife twice and then divorces her a third time for one thousand, the entire one thousand is in exchange for the remaining one divorce, by indication of intention. Similarly here. Unlike when the kitabah preceded, which is the issue that follows, because the badal is equivalent to the whole since there is no entitlement at that point in anything. So they differ.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the amount of badal (kitabah payment) that remains when a female slave is both a mudabbirah (given tadbir) and a mukatabah. The issue arises when the master dies, and the slave obtains freedom for one-third of her value through tadbir. The question is how much of the kitabah badal she must still pay. Imam Muhammad argues that the badal was set against the entire slave, but since she already has acquired freedom for one-third by tadbir, that one-third cannot be subject to payment. Therefore, one-third of the badal falls away, and she must only work (sa'y) to pay two-thirds of the kitabah price or two-thirds of her value, whichever is less. The Sahibayn argue that the badal is effectively against the remaining two-thirds of her value, so she must pay the full badal, but in practice she will choose the lesser of the two amounts. The commentary elaborates on the reasoning, including an analogy with divorce: if a man divorces his wife twice and then divorces her a third time for a sum, the entire sum is understood to be for the final divorce. Similarly, the intention here restricts the badal to the portion not already freed. The passage distinguishes the case where kitabah precedes tadbir, which is treated differently.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with her master to earn her freedom by paying a specified sum.
مدبرة (mudabbirah): A female slave who has been promised freedom upon her master's death through the contract of tadbir.
بدل الكتابة (badal al-kitabah): The payment (price) agreed upon in the kitabah contract that the slave must pay to earn freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a mudabbirah mukatabah's master dies with no other property, how much of the kitabah badal must she pay?
A) The entire badal
B) Two-thirds of the badal
C) One-third of the badal
D) She pays nothing

Key Takeaway
The amount of kitabah badal drops by one-third according to Imam Muhammad when the slave already has a tadbir entitlement to that portion; the Sahibayn reject any reduction.

Tadbir of a Mukatabah and Her Subsequent Choices
Ruling on tadbir of a mukatabah and subsequent options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a master makes a mukatabah a mudabbirah, identify her options, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the amount she must pay after the master's death.

Core Idea
Tadbir of a mukatabah is valid; she may continue kitabah or cancel it; after master's death she has a choice according to Abu Hanifa, but Sahibayn mandate the lesser amount.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a scenario where a master makes his already mukatabah (under a kitabah contract) slave also a mudabbirah (subject to tadbir). The central ruling is that the tadbir is valid, and the slave retains a choice to either continue the kitabah or cancel it by declaring incapacity (ta'jiz), becoming solely a mudabbirah. The passage then presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding her obligation if she chooses to continue the kitabah and the master dies with no other property. Finally, it covers the case of direct manumission of a mukatab by the master, clarifying that the kitabah badal falls away.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling on tadbir of a mukatabah
Note that the tadbir is valid (sahih) because ownership remains with the master during kitabah. The slave is given a choice: either continue on the kitabah or cancel it by ta'jiz and become a mudabbirah. Understand the reason: kitabah is not binding on the slave (ghayr lazim).
This ruling is settled (zahir al-riwayah) with no ikhtilaf.
2
Analyze the scenario: she continues kitabah and master dies without other property
If she continues kitabah and the master dies with no other assets except the slave herself (as a mudabbirah), then the question of what she must pay (sa'y) arises. The amount is two-thirds of something because one-third is freed via tadbir.
Two-thirds of either the kitabah price or her value; the dispute is over whether she has a choice.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds she has a genuine choice (khiyar) between paying two-thirds of the kitabah price or two-thirds of her value. The Sahibayn argue she must pay the lesser of the two because the choice is meaningless; the 'agreed amount' is the lesser.
The imams agree on the existence of a dispute over choice, not over the amount calculation.
4
Examine the ruling on direct manumission of a mukatab
If the master frees the mukatab (i'taq), the manumission is valid immediately because ownership remains. The kitabah badal drops because it was undertaken in exchange for freedom, which is now granted directly. The contract is annulled with the slave's presumed consent.
This ruling is also from zahir al-riwayah and uncontested.
5
Apply the legal principles
Distinguish between the two contracts: kitabah (binding on master, not on slave) and tadbir (a promise of freedom upon death). Understand that the master can override the kitabah by manumission, and the slave can cancel it by ta'jiz.
These principles reflect the Hanafi view of ownership and contractual flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آقا نے مکاتبہ کو مد برہ بنا دیا تو تدبیر مسیح ہے اسے اختیار ہے چاہے مکاتبہ رہے چاہے خود کو عاجز کر کے مدبرہ ہو جائے
قال وان دبر مكاتبة صح التدبير لما بينا ولها الخيار ان شاءت مضت على الكتابة وان شاءت عجزت نفسها وصارت مدبرة لان الكتابة ليست بلازمة فى جانب الهملوك فان مضت على كتابتها فمات المولى ولا مال له غيرها فهى بالخيار ان شاءت سعت في ثلثى مال الكتابة او ثلثي قيمتها عند ابي حنيفة وقالا تسعى في الاقل منهما فالخلاف في هذا الفصل فى الخيار بناء على ما ذكرنا اما المقدار فمتفق عليه ووجهه ما بينا . قال . واذا اعتق المولى مكاتبه عتق باعتاقه لقيام ملكه فيه وسقط بدل الكتابة لانه ما التزمه الا مقابلا بالعتق وقد حصل له دونه فلا يلزمه والكتابة وان كانت لازمة فى جانب المولى ولكنها تفسخ برضاء العبد والظاهر رضاه توسلا الى عتقه بغير بدل مع سلامة الاكساب له لانا نبقى الكتابة في حقه
ترجمہ اور اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ کو مد روکا تو تو ہی مسیح ہے اور اسکو اختیار ہے۔ چاہے کتابت پر چلے اور چاہے خود کو عاجز کر کے مد برہ ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ کتابت لازمی نہیں ہوتی جانب مملوک میں۔ پس اگر وہ کتابت پر چلی اور آقا مر گیا اور اس کے علاوہ کچھ مال نہیں تو اس کو اختبار ہے چاہے دو تہائی مال کتابت میں سعایت کرے چاہے اپنی قیمت کے دو تہائی میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ صاحبہیں فرماتے ہیں
If the master makes his mukatabah a mudabbirah, the tadbir is valid. She has the choice: if she wishes, she may continue on the kitabah; if she wishes, she may declare herself incapable (ta'jiz) and become a mudabbirah. Because the kitabah is not binding on the side of the slave. If she continues on her kitabah and the master dies with no other property, she has the choice: if she wishes, she may work for two-thirds of the kitabah price, or two-thirds of her value according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: she works for the lesser of the two. The dispute in this section is on the choice based on what we mentioned. As for the amount, it is agreed upon, and its reason is what we explained. He said: If the master frees his mukatab, he becomes free by his freeing because his ownership over him remains, and the kitabah badal drops because he only undertook it in exchange for freedom, and he has obtained it without it, so it is not binding. The kitabah, although binding on the side of the master, is annulled with the slave's consent, and it is apparent that he consents to attain freedom without payment while preserving his earnings, because we keep the kitabah in his favor?
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings related to mukatab. First, it addresses the scenario where a master makes his female slave who is already a mukatabah (under kitabah contract) also a mudabbirah (given tadbir). The tadbir is valid, and the slave has a choice: she can either continue on the kitabah contract or cancel it by declaring herself incapable (ta'jiz) and become solely a mudabbirah. This is because kitabah is not binding on the slave; she can unilaterally cancel it. If she continues on kitabah and the master dies with no other property, then she has a choice as to how she will pay off her obligation. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, she may choose to work (sa'y) to pay either two-thirds of the kitabah price or two-thirds of her market value. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say she must work for the lesser of the two amounts, so she has no real choice; the lesser is forced. The dispute here is about whether she has a choice (khiyar) or not, but they agree on the amount: she pays two-thirds of whichever is less. The second ruling is about the master directly freeing (i'taq) his mukatab. Since the master still holds ownership over the slave (the kitabah does not transfer ownership), the manumission is valid and effective immediately. The badal (kitabah payment) drops because it was only undertaken in exchange for freedom, and now freedom is granted without it. The kitabah contract is dissolved by the slave's consent, which is presumed because he gains immediate freedom without further payment and also gains the right to keep his earnings (since the kitabah falls away).

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A contract where the master promises freedom to his slave upon his death, from one-third of his estate.
عجزت نفسها (ajazat nafsaha): She declared herself incapable (ta'jiz) of fulfilling the kitabah contract, thereby canceling it and becoming solely a mudabbirah.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave by the master's act, which is valid despite an existing kitabah contract because ownership remains.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master makes his mukatabah also a mudabbirah, what options does she have?
A) She must continue the kitabah
B) She may continue kitabah or cancel it and become solely a mudabbirah
C) She must become a mudabbirah
D) The tadbir is invalid

Key Takeaway
Combining tadbir with kitabah is valid; the slave has initial options, and an intra-Hanafi dispute exists on the post-death obligation.

Ruling When Master Makes Mukatabah a Mudabbirah
Explains the ruling and ikhtilaf when a mukatabah is made mudabbirah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mukatabah is made mudabbirah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the slave's choice upon the master's death.

Core Idea
A mukatabah made mudabbirah has an initial choice; upon the master's death, Abu Hanifa grants a further choice while the Sahibayn fix the lesser amount.

This lesson examines a nuanced case at the intersection of two slave emancipation contracts: kitabah and tadbir. When a master first enters a kitabah contract with a female slave and later makes her a mudabbirah, Islamic law must reconcile the two rights. The Hanafi school agrees that the tadbir is valid and the slave may choose to continue or renounce the kitabah. However, a dispute arises if she continues and the master dies insolvent: must she work (sa'y) to pay two-thirds of the kitabah or two-thirds of her value? Imam Abu Hanifa gives her a choice; the two Sahibayn oblige her to the lesser amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario and ruling
The master makes his mukatabah (female slave under kitabah) a mudabbirah. The tadbir is valid. She has an immediate choice: continue the kitabah or declare inability and become a mudabbirah only. Note that kitabah is not binding on the slave in the Hanafi school.
2
Focus on the case after master's death
If she continues the kitabah and the master dies leaving no property except her, then she must perform sa'y to cover the owed amount. All Hanafi authorities agree that only two-thirds of the original kitabah or her value is due because one-third is dropped due to the tadbir.
3
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she has a choice: she may perform sa'y for two-thirds of the kitabah payment or two-thirds of her market value. The rationale is that the kitabah payment is for the entire freedom, but the tadbir already secures one-third freedom, so she can choose which basis to pay.
This is based on the principle that the consideration (badal) is for the portion of freedom not already obtained.
4
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that she does not have a choice; she must perform sa'y for the lesser of the two amounts. Their reasoning: since she already has a claim to one-third freedom, the liability should be minimized to avoid imposing more than necessary.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and agreement
The practical difference is that under Abu Hanifa she chooses the smaller burden (so outcome is same), but the principle differs: she has a right to elect the basis of payment. The amount itself is agreed: two-thirds of either value. Later scholars discuss whether she can force ta'jiz if master refuses.
The commentary notes a secondary dispute among mashayikh on ta'jiz.

Source Text

قال وان دبر مكاتبة صح التدبير لما بينا ولها الخيار ان شاءت مضت على الكتابة وان شاءت عجزت نفسها وصارت مدبرة لان الكتابة ليست بلازمة فى جانب الهملوك فان مضت على كتابتها فمات المولى ولا مال له غيرها فهى بالخيار ان شاءت سعت في ثلثى مال الكتابة او ثلثي قيمتها عند ابي حنيفة وقالا تسعى في الاقل منهما فالخلاف في هذا الفصل فى الخيار بناء على ما ذكرنا اما المقدار فمتفق عليه ووجهه ما بينا .
ترجمہ اور اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ کو مد روکا تو تو ہی مسیح ہے اور اسکو اختیار ہے۔ چاہے کتابت پر چلے اور چاہے خود کو عاجز کر کے مد برہ ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ کتابت لازمی نہیں ہوتی جانب مملوک میں۔ پس اگر وہ کتابت پر چلی اور آقا مر گیا اور اس کے علاوہ کچھ مال نہیں تو اس کو اختبار ہے چاہے دو تہائی مال کتابت میں سعایت کرے چاہے اپنی قیمت کے دو تہائی میں امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ صاحبہیں فرماتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں سے مکمتر میں سعایت کرے۔ پس اس فصل میں اختلاف صرف اختیار میں ہے۔ بنا بر آنکہ ہم ذکر کر چکے۔ رہی مقدار سواس پر اتفاق ہے اور وجہ وہی ہے۔ جو ہم نے بیان کی۔
تشریح قوله وان دبر مكاتبته ... الخ - اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ باندی کومد برہ کیا تو بدلیل مذکور (انه تلقتها جهتا حریة ) مد بر کرنا صحیح ہے۔ اب اس مکاتبہ مدبرہ کو اختیار ہے چاہے عقد کتابت پورا کر لے چاہے خود کو عاجز کر کے مدبرہ ہو جائے ۔ اس لئے کہ احناف وائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک عقد کتابت مملوک کی جانب میں لازمی نہیں ہوتا ۔ پھر ذخیرہ میں ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کی بابت مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے کہ جب مکاتب خود کو عاجز قرار دینا چاہے اور آقا اس کو نہ مانے تو اس سے کتابت فسخ ہو جائے گی یا نہیں؟ سومحمد بن سلمہ کہتے ہیں کہ آقا اگر اس کی تعجیز کا انکار کرے تو اس کو اس کا اختیار ہے۔ لیکن شیخ ابو بکر بنی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ بات اس کے بالکل خلاف ہے جو ہمارے اصحاب نے اپنی کتابوں میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ اس میں غلام خود مختار ہے۔
He said: If the master makes his mukatabah a mudabbirah, the tadbir is valid for the reason we mentioned. She has a choice: if she wishes she may continue on the kitabah, and if she wishes she may declare her inability and become a mudabbirah, because the kitabah is not binding on the side of the slave. Then if she continues on her kitabah, and the master dies and he has no property besides her, then she has a choice: if she wishes she may work (sa'y) for two-thirds of the kitabah payment or two-thirds of her value according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: she works for the lesser of the two. So the difference in this section is with respect to the choice, based on what we mentioned. As for the amount, there is agreement on it, and its justification is what we explained. Translation: And if the master made his mukatabah a mudabbirah, then the tadbir is valid, and she has the choice: either she continues on the kitabah or she declares herself incapable and becomes a mudabbirah, because the kitabah is not binding upon the slave. Then if she continues on her kitabah and the master dies and has no property other than her, then she has a choice: either she works (sa'y) for two-thirds of the kitabah payment or two-thirds of her value according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two masters (Sahibayn) say: she works for the lesser of the two. So in this section the difference is only in the choice, based on what we have mentioned. As for the amount, there is agreement upon it, and the reason is what we have stated. Commentary: He said 'and if he makes his mukatabah a mudabbirah...' - If the master made his mukatabah slave-girl a mudabbirah, then by the mentioned proof (that two aspects of freedom have met) the tadbir is valid. Now this mukatabah mudabbirah has a choice: either she completes the contract of kitabah or she declares herself incapable and becomes a mudabbirah. This is because according to the Hanafis and the three Imams, the contract of kitabah is not binding on the side of the slave. Then in al-Dhakhirah it is mentioned that there is a difference among the mashayikh concerning this issue: when the mukatab wants to declare his inability and the master refuses, is the kitabah annulled or not? Muhammad ibn Salama says: if the master rejects his declaration of inability, he still has the choice. But Shaykh Abu Bakr (al-Balkhi) says that this is completely contrary to what our companions have mentioned in their books, that the slave is independent in this matter.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the case where a master makes his female slave who is already a mukatabah (i.e., under a kitabah contract to purchase her freedom) into a mudabbirah (i.e., a slave whose freedom is postponed until the master's death). The ruling covers two scenarios: first, the validity of the tadbir act itself, and second, the choices available to the slave if the master dies insolvent. The author of the Hidayah, quoted here, begins by stating that the tadbir is valid because both direction of freedom have converged (i.e., the kitabah and the tadbir both aim at freedom). The mukatabah then has an immediate choice: she may continue the kitabah contract or she may declare herself unable to pay (ta'jiz) and revert to being a pure mudabbirah, since the kitabah is not binding on the slave's side in the Hanafi school (unlike some other schools). The dispute arises when she chooses to continue the kitabah and then the master dies leaving no property except her. At that point, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, she has a choice: either she works (sa'y) to pay two-thirds of the kitabah payment, or she works to pay two-thirds of her market value. According to the Sahibayn, she does not have this choice; rather, she must perform sa'y for the lesser of these two amounts. All agree that only two-thirds of the payment is due, because one-third of the kitabah payment is considered dropped due to the tadbir (since she already has a right to freedom from one-third of her value through the tadbir). The reasoning, as explained in the commentary, is that the consideration (badal) in the kitabah contract is ostensibly for the entire slave's freedom, but in meaning it is only for the portion that is not already due for emancipation. The commentary also notes a secondary dispute among later Hanafi scholars regarding whether the slave can force the annulment of the kitabah by declaring inability if the master refuses.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave who has entered into a kitabah contract to purchase her freedom by paying fixed installments.
مدبرة (mudabbirah): A slave whose emancipation is postponed to after the master's death (tadbir).
سعاية (sa'yah): Work performed by a slave to earn money to pay the kitabah or to compensate the master's estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the agreed-upon fraction that the slave must work for (sa'y) when the master dies insolvent?
A) 1/3
B) 2/3
C) 1/2
D) Full amount

Key Takeaway
When a mukatabah is made mudabbirah, the tadbir is valid; if she continues kitabah and the master dies insolvent, she works for two-thirds; Abu Hanifa gives a choice of basis, the Sahibayn fix the lesser.
