Kitabah for a Female Slave and Her Children
Expands kitabah ruling for a female slave and her two young children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a female slave contracting kitabah for herself and her young children, and explain why payment by any one of them frees all without recourse.

Core Idea
A female slave may validly contract kitabah for herself and her young children; payment by any one frees all with no right of recourse.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a female slave who enters a kitabah contract covering herself and her two young children. The translation makes the basic ruling clear: it is permissible, and if any one of them pays the kitabah price, all become free, and that payer cannot seek reimbursement from the others. The commentary then clarifies three important points: the nature of the contract, the applicability to both male and female slaves, and the legal principle of principality and dependence (asalah wa taba'iyyah) that governs the relationship between the mother and her children. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the Hanafi position on the capacity of a female slave to contract for her dependents despite lacking full guardianship (wilayah) over them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a kitabah contract by a female slave on herself and her two young sons. The ruling stated at the outset is that it is valid and permissible.
The base text is from al-Hidayah.
2
Understand the principal-dependent relationship
The mother is the principal (asl) and the children are dependents (tabi'). Because they are included in her contract, payment by any of them fulfills the contract for all, and no recourse is allowed between them.
This is the key to the 'no recourse' rule.
3
Resolve the guardianship concern
The placement of this ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir in the context of a female slave confirms that it applies equally to male and female slaves, removing any doubt that it might be specific to a father who has guardianship. The mother does not need guardianship; she simply includes them as dependents.
Otherwise, one might think a female slave cannot do this.
4
Apply to the scenario with two children
The case is set with two children to illustrate that if only one child were in the contract, one might mistakenly think each child is independent and payment by one frees only that child. With two children, the dependency relationship is clear, and payment by either frees both.
The two-child case removes ambiguity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله واذا كاتبت الامة .... الخ ۔ مسئلہ کا حکم اور اس کا مفہوم ترجمہ سے واضح ہے مزید وضاحت کی ضرورت نہیں۔ البتہ یہاں چند امور قابل لحاظ ہیں۔ اول یه كه كاتبت الامة على نفسها بمعنى قبلت عقد الكتابة على نفسها وعلى ابنين صغيرين لھا ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ شیخ ابو جعفر نے کشف الغوامض میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ مبسوط میں اس مسئلہ کی وضع غلام کے حق میں رکھی گئی ہے اور جامع صغیر میں اس کی وضع باندی کے حق میں رکھی ہے۔ اس کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر جامع صغیر کی روایت نہ ہوتی تو مبسوط کی وضع پر یہ وہم ہوسکتا تھا کہ ممکن ہے جواز اس لئے ہو کہ باپ کو صغیر پر ولایت حاصل ہے۔ اور ماں کو یہ ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے باندی کی صورت میں جواز نہ ہوگا۔ پس جامع صغیر کی روایت سے یہ واضح ہو گیا کہ حکم مذکور غلام اور باندی دونوں کے حق میں برابر ہے۔ سوم یہ کہ مسئلہ کی وضع دو صغیر بچوں کے حق میں رکھنے سے یہ فائدہ ہوا کہ ان میں سے جو بھی عوض ادا کر دے وہ دوسرے پر رجوع نہیں کر سکتا اور وہ دونوں آزاد ہو جائیں گے۔ اگر مسئلہ کی وضع صرف ایک صغیر کے حق میں ہوتی تو اس جیسی صورت میں کوئی کہ سکتا تھا کہ اگر دو بیٹوں میں سے ایک بیٹا بدل کتابت ادا کر دے تو دوسرا بیٹا آزا انہیں نا چاہیے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں نہ اصالت ہے نہ تبعیت ۔
His saying: 'And if the female slave contracts kitabah...' The ruling of the case and its meaning are clear from the translation; no further explanation is needed. However, there are several points to note. First: 'The female slave contracted kitabah upon herself' means she accepted the kitabah contract upon herself and upon her two young sons. Second: Shaykh Abu Ja'far mentioned in Kashf al-Ghawamid that in al-Mabsut, this case is placed in the context of a male slave, and in al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is placed in the context of a female slave. The benefit of this is that if the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir were not present, one might have thought that the permissibility (in al-Mabsut) is because the father has guardianship over the young child, whereas the mother does not have such guardianship. Therefore, permissibility would not apply in the case of the female slave. So the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir clarifies that the mentioned ruling is equal for both male and female slaves. Third: Placing the case with two young children yields the benefit that whichever of them pays the consideration cannot take recourse against the other, and both of them will be freed. If the case had been placed with only one young child, then in a situation like (where there are two sons), someone could say that if one son pays the kitabah price, the other son should not be freed because there is neither principality nor dependence between them.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling when a female slave enters a kitabah contract for herself and her two young children. The translation makes the basic ruling clear: it is permissible, and if any one of them pays, all are freed, and that payer cannot take recourse against the others. The commentary then highlights three important points. First, it defines the contract: the female slave accepts kitabah upon herself and her two sons. Second, it notes a difference in the placement of this case between al-Mabsut (where it is presented for a male slave) and al-Jami' al-Saghir (where it is presented for a female slave). This difference is crucial because if only al-Mabsut's version existed, one might think the permissibility is specific to a father who has guardianship over his children, which a mother lacks. Al-Jami' al-Saghir's version confirms that the ruling applies equally to a female slave. Third, the case is set with two children to illustrate that if one pays, the other is also freed without recourse, because they are included in the mother's contract as dependents. If there were only one child, confusion could arise when two children are present—one might think each child is independent and payment by one frees only himself.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitabah): A contract of manumission by which a slave pays a fixed sum to the master and becomes free upon completion.
ولایت (wilayah): Legal guardianship over minors, which the father has but the mother generally does not in Hanafi law.
اصالت و تبعیت (asalah wa taba'iyyah): Principality and dependence in a contract. Here, the mother is principal and children are dependents, so payment by any frees all without recourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator mention that al-Jami' al-Saghir places the case of kitabah for oneself and children in the context of a female slave?
A) To show that only male slaves can make such a contract.
B) To confirm that the ruling applies equally to male and female slaves.
C) To indicate that the mother does not need guardianship.
D) To limit the ruling to female slaves only.

Key Takeaway
A female slave may validly contract kitabah for herself and her young children, and payment by any one of them frees all without the right of recourse, based on the principle of principality and dependence.

Kitabah of a Jointly-Owned Slave: Divisibility and Payment Rights
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divisibility of kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the divisibility of kitabah and apply the ruling to determine who keeps payments received from a jointly-owned slave who becomes unable to pay.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: kitabah is divisible like manumission; Sahibayn: it is indivisible like a contract.

This passage presents a classic intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The issue arises when one co-owner of a slave authorizes the other to write a kitabah contract for his share, and the slave later becomes unable to pay. The core question: who keeps the payments already received? The answer hinges on whether the contract of kitabah is divisible (tatajazzā) or not, a debate rooted in analogy to manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
Two co-owners (Zayd and Amr) own a slave. Zayd authorizes Amr to write kitabah for Zayd's share (for 1000 dirhams) and collect payments. Amr writes the kitabah and collects part of the payment. Then the slave becomes unable to pay the remaining amount. Who gets the money Amr collected?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
According to Abu Hanifa, the payments belong solely to Amr (the authorized partner). The basis is that kitabah is divisible (tatajazzā), analogous to manumission. Therefore, the contract is valid only for Zayd's share, and Zayd, by authorizing and not participating, is considered a benefactor (mutabarri').
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to itq (manumission) where one co-owner can free his share alone.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the payments are shared between both co-owners. They argue kitabah is indivisible, so authorization for a share implies authorization for the entire slave. Thus, Amr acts as principal for his half and agent for Zayd's half. The slave becomes a mukatab between both owners, and payments are shared.
The Sahibayn treat kitabah as a contract of exchange, similar to a sale or ijara, which are indivisible.
4
Understand the role of authorization
Authorization (idhn) removes the right of rescission (faskh) from the non-writing co-owner. Without authorization, the other co-owner could rescind the kitabah. Here, Zayd's authorization also implies permission for the slave to pay, making him a benefactor under Abu Hanifa's view.
This is a key nuance: authorization changes the legal relationship.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under the mufta bihi position (Abu Hanifa), the authorized partner keeps all collected payments. Under the Sahibayn, payments are divided equally. This affects the financial outcome when the slave defaults.
The text indicates that Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon one (mufta bihi).

فائدہ .... اگر ایک شریک نے دوسرے شریک کو کتابت کی اجازت دے دی تو کتابت جائز ہوگی (امام مالک کا اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی کا اس میں اختلاف ہے ) اور ہمارے نزدیک بلا اجازت بھی جائز ہے۔ لیکن اس صورت میں دوسرے شریک کو نقص کتابت کا اختیار ہوگا۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہ ہوگی ) امام احمد حسن اور ابن ابی لیلی کے نزدیک بلا اجازت کتابت جائز ہوگی اور دوسرے شریک کو نقص کتابت کا اختیار نہ ہوگا ۔
This chapter is about the kitabah of a jointly-owned slave. The commentary says: The connection is that non-shared ownership is the norm, and sharing is contrary to the norm, so it is appropriate to mention the contrary after the norm. Some commentators said that mentioning kitabah of two after one is because one comes before two. This reasoning does not apply to the first issue of the chapter according to Abu Hanifa. A slave is jointly owned by two persons; one authorized his partner to write kitabah for his share for a thousand dirhams and collect the payment. He wrote kitabah and collected some of the thousand, then the slave became unable. The money belongs to the one who collected according to Abu Hanifa. The two disciples said: He is a mukatab between them, and what he paid is between them. The basis is that kitabah is divisible in his view, contrary to them, like manumission because it grants freedom in some respect, so it is confined to his share according to him due to divisibility. The benefit of authorization is that he does not have the right of rescission as he would have if he did not authorize. And his authorization for him to receive the payment is permission for the slave to pay, so he is a benefactor of his share upon him. Therefore, everything received is for him. In their view, authorization to write kitabah for his share is authorization to write kitabah for the entire slave due to non-divisibility. So he is principal in half and agent in half. Thus, the slave is a mukatab between them, and the received payment is shared between them, remaining so after inability. Explanation: A slave is shared between Zayd and Amr. Zayd said to Amr: Write kitabah for my share for a thousand dirhams and collect the payment. Amr did so and collected some payment. Then the slave became unable to pay the rest. The payment Amr collected is his according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two disciples, the slave is a mukatab between them, and what he paid is for both of them. The author of al-Hidayah says the basis of this difference is that kitabah is divisible (can be split) according to Abu Hanifa, and not divisible according to the Sahibayn. And similarly in manumission, kitabah is like manumission because it also grants freedom in some sense. So according to Abu Hanifa, the kitabah is confined to the share of the one who wrote it. Some commentators mentioned that in some manuscripts 'between two men' is replaced by 'between two partners', and this is preferable because the ruling is general. The phrase 'two partners' includes both men and women. Then the commentator discusses the benefit of authorization. Then a benefit: If one partner authorizes the other to write kitabah, it is permissible (Imam Malik and in one narration Imam Shafi'i differ). In our view, it is permissible without authorization, but then the other partner has the right to rescind the kitabah. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i say it is not permissible without authorization. Imam Ahmad, Hasan, and Ibn Abi Layla say it is permissible without authorization and the other partner does not have the right to rescind.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the kitabah of a jointly-owned slave when one co-owner authorizes the other to write kitabah for his share. The central issue is whether the contract of kitabah is divisible (tatajazzu) or indivisible. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that kitabah is divisible because it is akin to manumission, which is also divisible. Therefore, when a co-owner authorizes his partner to write kitabah for his share only, the contract is valid for that share alone. The authorized partner, who acts as the agent for the authorizing partner, receives the payments. If the slave later becomes unable to pay, the money collected belongs solely to the authorized partner because the authorizing partner is considered a benefactor (mutabarri') with respect to his share. In contrast, the two disciples hold that kitabah is indivisible, so authorization to write kitabah for one's share necessarily authorizes kitabah for the entire slave. Consequently, the authorized partner acts as principal in half (his own share) and agent in half (the other partner's share). The slave becomes a mukatab between both owners, and any payments received are shared between them. This difference persists even after the slave becomes unable to pay. The passage then clarifies the benefit of authorization: without it, the non-participating co-owner would have the right to rescind the kitabah; with authorization, he loses that right. Finally, a note is added comparing the Hanafi position with other schools on the permissibility of kitabah without the other co-owner's permission. According to the Hanafi school, kitabah without permission is valid, but the non-consenting co-owner retains the right to rescind. This contrasts with the view of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, who deem it invalid, and the view of Imam Ahmad, Hasan, and Ibn Abi Layla, who deem it valid without any right of rescission.

Key Terms
كتابة (مكاتبة) (kitābah (mukātabah)): A contract whereby a slave agrees to pay a sum to the master in exchange for freedom upon payment.
تجزى (تتجزى) (tatajazzā): The property of being divisible; here, whether the contract of kitabah can be valid for only a share of the slave.
اذن (idhn): Permission given by one co-owner to the other to perform an act (here, write kitabah and collect payment).
فسخ (faskh): Right to rescind or annul the kitabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, according to the relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa), if one co-owner authorizes the other to write kitabah for his share and the slave becomes unable to pay, what happens to the payments already collected?
A) The payments are divided equally between both co-owners.
B) The payments belong entirely to the authorized partner who collected them.
C) The payments are returned to the slave.
D) The payments go to charity.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of kitabah determines whether payments from a jointly-owned slave belong solely to the authorized partner (Abu Hanifa) or are shared (Sahibayn); the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.

intermediate
8 min
Kitabah of a Co-Owned Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Divisibility
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divisibility of kitabah for co-owned slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of kitabah for a co-owned slave, explain the qiyas to itq, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to determine payment distribution.

Core Idea
Kitabah is divisible like itq: only the writing partner's share is affected.

When two partners jointly own a slave, and one partner writes a kitabah (contract of manumission by payment) for his share with the other's permission, a dispute arises if the slave fails to pay. Who owns the collected payments? Abu Hanifa says the writing partner alone; the Sahibayn say both share. This lesson unpacks the root of their disagreement: the nature of kitabah's divisibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Recognize that the dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Both agree the kitabah is valid, but differ on the effect when the slave cannot complete payment.
The permission from the non-writing partner is presumed; without it, the kitabah is subject to annulment.
2
Extract the Root Cause: Divisibility of Kitabah
According to the text, the difference stems from whether kitabah is 'mutajazzi' (divisible). Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible, so it applies only to the share of the partner who wrote it. The Sahibayn hold it is not divisible, so it binds both partners' shares as a single contract.
The same disagreement exists for itq (manumission) of a co-owned slave.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's Qiyas to Itq
Abu Hanifa analogizes kitabah to itq: just as manumission of a share in a co-owned slave is effective only on the manumitting partner's share (divisible), so too kitabah, because both are paths to freedom. Therefore, the kitabah contract and its payments belong solely to the writing partner.
The illa (effective cause) is that both itq and kitabah are 'tariq al-'itq' (ways of emancipation).
4
Understand the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The practical difference: if the slave fails to pay, the amount already collected goes to the writing partner alone (Abu Hanifa) or is shared between both partners (Sahibayn). The non-writing partner cannot revoke the kitabah because he gave permission.
This affects the distribution of funds upon the slave's inability to complete payment.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi (Relied-Upon) Position
The Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's view. The text presents Abu Hanifa's reasoning first and the analogy to itq, implying it is the stronger opinion. Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Marghinani) adopt this as the operative ruling.
This position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is considered al-mu'tamad.

شرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳ سے میرے حصہ کو ہزار درہم کے عوض مکاتب کر کے بدل کتابت وصول کرلے۔ عمرو نے ایسا ہی کیا اور غلام سے کچھ بدل کتابت وصول بھی کر لیا۔ مگر باقی بدل کی ادائیگی سے غلام عاجز ہو گیا۔ تو عمرو نے جو بدل کتابت وصول کیا ہے۔ وہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا ہوگا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک غلام دونوں کے درمیان مکاتب ہوگا ۔ اور جو کچھ بدل ادا کیا ہے وہ بھی دونوں کا ہوگا ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس اختلاف کی اصل یہ ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کتابت متجری ہے۔ یعنی اس کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک متجری نہیں ہے۔ جیسے اعتاق میں بھی ایسا ہی اختلاف ہے تو کتابت بمنزلہ اعتاق ہے۔ کیونکہ کتابت کے ذریعہ سے بھی ایک راہ سے آزادی حاصل ہوتی ہے بایں معنی کہ وہ قبضہ کے لحاظ سے آزاد ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کتابت اس شریک کے حصہ پر رہے گی جس نے مکاتب کیا ہے۔
قوله بين رجلين .... الخ بعض شراح نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ بعض نسخوں میں بین رجلین کے بجائے بین شریکین ہے۔ اور یہی اولیٰ ہے۔ بقول صاحب نتائج وجہ اولویت یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کا حکم عام ہے۔ غلام دو مردوں میں مشترک ہو یا ایک مرد اور ایک عورت کے درمیان یا دو عورتوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو اور لفظ شریکین سب کو شامل ہے یا تو بایں معنی کہ شریک بروزن فعیل بمعنی مفعول ہے۔ اور شرکہ فی کذا سے ہے۔ اور فعیل بمعنی مفعول میں مذکر و مؤنث دونوں یکساں ہوتے ہیں۔ یا بایں معنی کہ لفظ شریک اسماء جامدہ میں شمار ہو گیا جیسے لفظ تابع وغیرہ کی بابت کہا گیا ہے اور اسی حیثیت سے توابع کو تابع کی جمع کہا گیا ہے نہیں یہ بھی مذکر و مؤنث ہر دو کو برابر شامل ہوگا۔ پھر صاحب عنایہ نے بین شریکین والا نسخہ ہی اختیار کیا ہے۔ جس کی تفسیر سعدی چلپی نے ای بین رجلین سے کی ہے۔ مگر یہ تفسیر بہت ہی عجیب ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جب اس مسئلہ کا حکم صرف اسی صورت کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہے کہ غلام دو مردوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو تو پھر لفظ شریکین جو رجلین اور غیر رجلین ہر دو کو عام ہے اس کی تفسیر د جلین کے ساتھ کرنا بے وجہ ہے۔
Book of al-Mukatab. Sharh Urdu Hidayah, Volume 13: 'He wrote kitabah for my share in exchange for a thousand dirhams and collected the kitabah payment. Amr did likewise and collected some kitabah payment from the slave. Then the slave became unable to pay the remaining payment. So according to Imam Abu Hanifa, what Amr collected of the kitabah payment is his. According to the Sahibayn, the slave is a mukatab between both of them, and whatever payment was made is also between both of them.' The author of Hidayah says that the basis of this difference is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, kitabah is divisible (mutajazzi), meaning its parts can be separated. According to the Sahibayn, it is not divisible. Just as there is similar difference in manumission (itq), so kitabah is analogous to manumission because through kitabah freedom is obtained in one way, meaning the slave becomes free in terms of possession. Therefore, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the kitabah remains on the share of the partner who wrote it. His statement 'between two men' (qawluhu bayna rajulayn)... some commentators have mentioned that in some manuscripts it is 'between two partners' (bayna sharikayn) instead of 'between two men', and this is preferable. According to the author of Nata'ij, the reason for preference is that the ruling of this case is general: whether the slave is jointly owned by two men, or between a man and a woman, or between two women, the word 'sharikayn' includes all. Either in the sense that 'sharik' is on the pattern of fa'eel in the meaning of maf'ool (passive), and it is from shirkah fi kadha, and fa'eel in the meaning of maf'ool is the same for masculine and feminine. Or in the sense that the word 'sharik' is counted among the non-derived nouns (asma' jamidah), as is said about the word 'tabi‘' etc., and in that capacity, 'tawabi‘' is the plural of 'tabi‘', so it likewise includes both masculine and feminine equally. Then the author of 'Inayah chose the reading 'bayna sharikayn'. Sa'di Chalpi interpreted it as 'bayna rajulayn', but this interpretation is very strange because the ruling of this case is not specific to the situation where the slave is jointly owned by two men, so the word 'sharikayn' which is general for both 'rajulayn' and non-'rajulayn' should not be interpreted as only 'rajulayn'.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a co-owned slave whose one partner writes a kitabah (contract of manumission by payment) for his share with the other partner's permission. The slave pays some amount but then becomes unable to pay the rest. The ruling: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the amount already collected belongs solely to the partner who wrote the kitabah. According to the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), the slave is a mukatab between both partners, so the collected amount belongs to both in proportion to their shares. The author of Hidayah explains that the root of the difference lies in whether the kitabah contract is divisible (mutajazzi). Abu Hanifa holds that it is divisible, meaning it can be split into separate contracts for each share. Therefore, the kitabah by one partner only affects his own share, and any payment goes to him. The Sahibayn hold that it is indivisible; thus the kitabah becomes a single contract binding both partners. This dispute mirrors a similar difference in manumission (itq) of a co-owned slave, so kitabah is analogized to itq. The text then discusses a textual variant: some manuscripts read 'between two partners' (sharikayn) rather than 'between two men' (rajulayn), and this is preferred because the ruling applies to any joint ownership, regardless of the partners' gender.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitabah): A contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave earns money to pay for his freedom in installments.
متجری (mutajazzi): Divisible; capable of being split into separate parts. Here, it refers to whether the kitabah contract can apply to only a partial share of a slave.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master and is earning his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the kitabah of a co-owned slave?
A) The divisibility vs. indivisibility of the kitabah contract
B) The ownership status of the slave
C) The validity of the permission given
D) The amount of payment received

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that kitabah is divisible like itq, so the writing partner alone owns the collected payments.

Authorization in Kitabah for a Co-Owned Slave
Inter-madhhab dispute on kitabah of co-owned slave without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a partner writing kitabah without permission and identify the legal effect of authorization on the right to annul.

Core Idea
Authorization removes the right to annul; without it, kitabah is valid but the other partner can annul.

When two people jointly own a slave, one may wish to write a kitabah (contract of manumission) for his share. Does he need the other partner's permission? And what are the consequences of acting without it? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on the benefit of authorization and compares it with other schools, highlighting the delicate balance between individual freedom and co-ownership rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The passage answers an implied question: if kitabah is divisible (per Abu Hanifa), what benefit does authorization provide? Recognize that authorization affects the right of the non-writing partner to annul the contract.
The concept of divisibility (tajzi) is central to the Hanafi view.
2
Understand the Hanafi position without authorization
According to the Hanafi school, kitabah without permission is valid (jaa'iz). However, the non-writing partner retains the right to annul (faskh) the contract. This protects his interest in the slave.
Validity does not require permission; the right to annul is the key consequence.
3
Analyze the effect of authorization
When the non-writing partner gives authorization, he forfeits his right to annul. Additionally, if he authorizes the writing partner to collect payments, it is as if he authorized the slave to pay, making the writing partner a benefactor; thus the collected amount belongs solely to the writing partner.
Authorization also impacts distribution of payments, as per Abu Hanifa.
4
Contrast with the Sahibayn view (divisibility of kitabah)
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold kitabah as indivisible. For them, authorizing kitabah for one's share amounts to authorizing the entire kitabah. The writing partner acts as principal for his half and agent for the other half; payments are shared.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference on the nature of kitabah.
5
Compare with other schools' rulings
Maliki and Shafi'i (one narration) hold kitabah without permission invalid. Ahmad, Hasan, and Ibn Abi Layla hold it valid with no right to annul. The Hanafi position stands between these extremes, balancing validity with a right to annul.
Understand the spectrum: some require consent, some give full validity, Hanafi gives validity with a conditional right to annul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وفائدة الاذن ... الخ - سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ جب امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک کتابت متجری ہے تو پھر ایک شریک کے دوسرے شریک کو کتابت کی اجازت دینے کا کیا فائدہ رہا۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اجازت دینے کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ جس شریک نے مکاتب نہیں کیا۔ اس کو فسخ کتابت کا اختیار حاصل نہ ہو جو بلا اجازت مکاتب کرنے کی صورت میں تھا۔ اور شریک کو عوض وصول کرنے کی اجازت دینا غلام کو ادا کرنے کی اجازت دینا ہے تو وہ غلام پر اپنے حصہ کا احسان کنندہ ہوا۔ اس لئے شریک نے جو کچھ وصول کیا ہے وہ سب اسی کا ہوا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اپنے حصہ کی کتابت کی اجازت دینا کل غلام مکاتب کرنے کی اجازت ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں کتابت متجزمی نہیں ہے۔ پس وہ نصف غلام مکاتب کرنے میں اصیل ہے۔ اور نصف میں شریک کی طرف سے وکیل ہے۔ لہذ اغلام دونوں کے درمیان مکاتب ہوا اور وکیل نے جو کچھ وصول کیا ہے وہ ان دونوں میں مشترک ہوگا۔ پھر غلام کے عاجز ہو جانے کے بعد بھی یونہی دونوں میں مشترک رہے گا۔
فائدہ .... اگر ایک شریک نے دوسرے شریک کو کتابت کی اجازت دے دی تو کتابت جائز ہوگی (امام مالک کا اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی کا اس میں اختلاف ہے ) اور ہمارے نزدیک بلا اجازت بھی جائز ہے۔ لیکن اس صورت میں دوسرے شریک کو نقص کتابت کا اختیار ہوگا۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز نہ ہوگی ) امام احمد حسن اور ابن ابی لیلی کے نزدیک بلا اجازت کتابت جائز ہوگی اور دوسرے شریک کو نقص کتابت کا اختیار نہ ہوگا ۔
His statement: 'And the benefit of authorization' ... is the answer to an implied question. The question is: When according to Imam Abu Hanifa kitabah is divisible, then what is the benefit of one partner giving authorization to the other for the kitabah? The summary of the answer is that the benefit of authorization is that the partner who did not write the kitabah does not have the right to annul the kitabah, which he would have had in the case of writing without authorization. And giving authorization to the partner to receive the payment is equivalent to giving permission to the slave to pay, so he becomes a benefactor to the slave regarding his share. Therefore, whatever the partner collected is all his. According to the Sahibayn, authorizing the kitabah of his share is authorization for the entire slave's kitabah, because in their view kitabah is indivisible. Hence, he is a principal (asil) in making half the slave a mukatab, and an agent (wakil) for the other half. Consequently, the slave becomes a mukatab between them, and what the agent collected is shared between them. After the slave becomes unable to pay, it remains shared between them. Benefit: If one partner gives authorization to the other for the kitabah, the kitabah is valid (Imam Malik and, in one narration, Imam al-Shafi'i differ on this). And according to us (Hanafis), it is also valid without authorization, but in that case the other partner has the right to annul the kitabah. According to Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, it is not valid without authorization. According to Imam Ahmad, Hasan, and Ibn Abi Layla, kitabah without authorization is valid and the other partner does not have the right to annul it.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage addresses a question: If kitabah is divisible (Abu Hanifa's view), why does a partner need to seek authorization from the other? The answer is that authorization removes the right of the non-writing partner to annul the kitabah. Without authorization, the non-writing partner could cancel the contract upon the slave's failure to pay. With authorization, he cannot annul it. Additionally, authorizing the writing partner to collect payment is like authorizing the slave to pay, making the writing partner a benefactor who owns the collected amount entirely. According to the Sahibayn (who hold kitabah is indivisible), authorization for the share amounts to authorization for the whole slave, making the writing partner an agent for the other half, so the payment is shared. The passage also provides a comparative note from other schools: The Hanafi school holds that kitabah without authorization is valid but the other partner can annul it. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i (in one narration) say it is invalid without authorization. Imam Ahmad, Hasan, and Ibn Abi Layla say it is valid and the other partner has no right of annulment. This shows the Hanafi position stands between these extremes.

Key Terms
اذن (idhn): Permission or authorization given by one partner to the other to write a kitabah for the entire slave or for the share.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or rescission of the kitabah contract by the non-writing partner.
اصیل (aseel): Principal; the person acting on his own behalf. Here, the writing partner is principal regarding his own share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a partner writes a kitabah for his share without the other partner's permission, what right does the other partner have?
A) He can cancel the kitabah (faskh)
B) He must accept the kitabah as binding
C) He can demand the entire payment from the writing partner
D) He has no rights concerning the kitabah

Key Takeaway
Kitabah without permission is valid in Hanafi law, but the non-writing partner retains the right to annul unless authorization was given.

Umm Walad of a Co-owned Mukatabah When Both Partners Claim Offspring
Ruling with qiyas to mudabbarah case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling of umm walad to a co-owned mukatabah slave-girl when both partners claim children, and explain the role of the kitabah contract's annulment.

Core Idea
A co-owned mukatabah becomes umm walad for the first claimant once the kitabah is annulled.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in Hanafi slave law: a female slave jointly owned by two men, both of whom make her a mukatabah. After each partner has intercourse with her and claims the resulting child, she fails to pay the kitabah. Who is her master as umm walad? The ruling turns on the nature of the kitabah contract and its temporary restriction on ownership transfer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of the slave before the events
The slave is co-owned by two partners, and both have entered into a mukatabah contract with her. This gives her a right to eventual freedom by paying installments, but she remains a slave during the contract.
Mukatabah: a contract of manumission by payment.
2
Analyze the first partner's claim of paternity
When the first partner has intercourse, she gives birth, and he claims the child. His claim is valid because he has partial ownership. His share of the slave becomes umm walad for him, but only his share, because the kitabah prevents transfer of ownership between partners.
Umm walad status is confined to his share initially.
3
Analyze the second partner's claim
The second partner also has intercourse, she gives birth, and he claims the child. His claim is also valid due to his apparent ownership. His share becomes umm walad for him as well.
Both shares are now umm walad for the respective claimant.
4
Determine the effect of her inability to pay
When she becomes unable to pay the kitabah, the kitabah contract is annulled (as if it never existed). This removes the obstacle that prevented full ownership transfer.
The obstacle (kitabah) is removed, allowing the first partner's prior intercourse to establish full umm walad status.
5
Conclude who becomes the full umm walad owner
After annulment, the entire slave-girl is revealed to be umm walad for the first claimant because his intercourse was earlier. The second claimant's share loses umm walad status, and the first claimant gains full rights.
The result is based on the removal of the kitabah restriction and the priority of the first intercourse.

قال و اذا كانت جارية بين رجلين كاتباها فوطيها احدهما فجاءت بولد فادعاه ثم وطيها الآخر فجائت بولد فادعاه ثم عجزت فهى ام ولد الاول لانه لما ادعى احدهما الولد صحت دعوته لقيام الملك له فيها وصار نصيبه ام ولد له لان المكاتبة لا تقبل النقل من ملك الى ملك فيقتصر امومية الولد على نصيبه كما في المدبرة المشتركة ولو ادعى الثانى ولدها الاخير صحت دعوته لقيام ملكه ظاهرا ثم اذا عجزت بعد ذلك جعلت الكتابة كان لم تكن وتبين ان الجارية كلها ام ولد للاول لانه زال المانع من الانتقال ووطيه سابق
ترجمہ ایک باندی دو آدمیوں میں مشترک ہے۔ جس کو انہوں نے مکاتب کر دیا پھر ایک نے اس سے وطی کی اور اس نے بچہ جنا۔ واطی نے اس کا دعوی کیا۔ پھر دوسرے نے ولی کی۔ اور بچہ ہوا اور دوسرے نے دعوی کیا پھر باندی عاجز ہو گئی تو وہ مدعی اول کی ام ولد ہوئی۔ کیونکہ جب ان میں سے ایک نے دعویٰ کیا تو اس کا دعوی صحیح ہو گیا با ندی میں اس کی ملک قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اس کا حصہ ام ولد ہو گیا کیونکہ مکاتبہ ایک ملک سے دوسرے ملک کی طرف منتقل ہونے کے قابل نہیں اتم ولد ہونا اسی کے حصہ پر منحصر رہے گا۔ جیسے مدبرہ مشترکہ میں ہے اور جب دوسرے نے دوسرے بچہ کا دعوی کیا تو اس کا دعوی بھی صحیح ہو ا بظاہر اس کی ملک قائم ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر جب اس کے بعد وہ عاجز ہوگئی تو کتابت کا لعدم کر دی گئی اور یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ پوری باندی پہلے مدعی کی ام ولد ہے کیونکہ منتقل ہونے سے مانع امرزائل ہو گیا۔ اور اسی کی وی سابق ہے۔
تشریح قوله واذا كانت الخ- ایک باندی دو شخصوں میں مشترک تھی اس کو دونوں نے مکاتب کر دیا۔ پھر ایک نے اس سے وطی کی اور بچہ ہوا اور واطی نے بچہ کا دعویٰ کیا کہ یہ میرا ہے پھر دوسرے نے ولی کی اس سے بھی بچہ ہوا اور اس نے بھی بچہ کا دعویٰ کیا اور باندی بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہوگئی تو باندی واطی اول کی اتم ولد ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جب ان میں سے ایک نے بچہ کا دعویٰ کیا تو قیام ملک کی وجہ سے اس کا دعویٰ صحیح ہوا اور اس کا حصہ ام ولد ہو گیا (بنابر آنکہ مکاتب میں استیلا دامام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک متجری ہوتا ہے ) کیونکہ مکا تبہ اس قابل نہیں ہوتی کہ ایک ملک سے دوسری ملک کی طرف منتقل ہو۔ پس ام ولد ہونا اس کے حصہ پر منحصر ہو گا جیسے ایک باندی دو میں مشترک تھی دونوں نے اس کو مد برہ کیا پھر ایک کی ولی سے بچہ ہوا اور واطی نے اس کا دعویٰ کیا تو نسب اس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اور امومیت بالا جماع اس کے حصہ پر منحصر رہتی ہے۔ قـولـه ولوادعى الثاني ..... الخ ۔ اور جب دوسرے شریک نے دعوی کیا تو اس کا دعوی بھی صحیح ہوا۔ کیونکہ ظاہر اس کی بھی ملک قائم ہے۔ لیکن جب باندی بدل کتابت سے عاجز ہوگئی تو کتابت کالعدم ہوگئی اور کل باندی مدعی کی ام ولد ہوگئی ۔ کیونکہ ام ولد ہونا جو اول کے حصہ تک محدود تھا وہ اس لئے تھا کہ مکاتب ایک ملک سے دوسری ملک کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوتا اور جب بوجہ بجز کتابت ختم ہوگئی تو یہ مافع زائل ہو گیا۔
He said: And if there is a female slave between two men who make her a mukatabah, then one of them has intercourse with her and she gives birth to a child and he claims it, then the other has intercourse with her and she gives birth to a child and he claims it, then she becomes unable (to pay), then she is the umm walad of the first claimant, because when one of them claimed the child, his claim is valid due to his established ownership in her, and his share becomes umm walad for him because the mukatabah does not allow transfer from one ownership to another, so the umm walad status is confined to his share, as in a co-owned mudabbarah. And if the second claimed her latter child, his claim is valid due to his apparent ownership. Then when she becomes unable after that, the kitabah is nullified and it becomes clear that the entire slave-girl is umm walad for the first, because the obstacle to transfer is removed and his intercourse was earlier. Translation: A slave-girl is jointly owned by two men. They make her a mukatabah. Then one has intercourse with her and she gives birth. The one who had intercourse claims the child. Then the second has intercourse and a child is born, and the second claims it. Then the slave-girl becomes unable to pay the kitabah. She becomes umm walad for the first claimant because when one of them claimed, his claim is valid due to his established ownership in her, and his share becomes umm walad for him, because a mukatabah is not capable of being transferred from one ownership to another, so umm walad status is confined to his share, as in a co-owned mudabbarah. And when the second claimed the latter child, his claim is also valid due to his apparent ownership. Then when she becomes unable thereafter, the kitabah is rendered as if it never existed, and it becomes clear that the entire slave-girl is umm walad for the first, because the obstacle to transfer has been removed and his intercourse was earlier. Commentary: Explanation of his statement 'and if there is a female slave...': A slave-girl is jointly owned by two individuals. Both make her a mukatabah. Then one has intercourse and she gives birth; the one who had intercourse claims the child saying it is his. Then the second has intercourse and also has a child, and he also claims the child. Then the slave-girl becomes unable to pay the kitabah payment. The slave-girl becomes umm walad for the first one who had intercourse. Because when one of them claimed the child, due to his ownership being established, his claim is valid and his share becomes umm walad (based on the fact that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the kitabah of a slave is divisible), because a mukatabah is not capable of being transferred from one ownership to another. So umm walad status is confined to his share, just like if a slave-girl is co-owned and both make her mudabbarah, then one has intercourse and a child is born, the child's lineage is established from him, and umm walad status is confined to his share by consensus. His statement 'and if the second claims...': And when the second partner claimed, his claim also becomes valid because his ownership is also apparent. But when the slave-girl becomes unable to pay the kitabah, the kitabah becomes null and void, and the entire slave-girl becomes umm walad for the first claimant. Because the umm walad status was confined to the first's share only because a mukatab cannot be transferred from one ownership to another, and when the kitabah ends due to her inability, that obstacle disappears.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This is a ruling regarding a co-owned female slave (jariyah) who is made mukatabah by both partners. After becoming a mukatabah, each partner has intercourse with her, and each claims the resulting child. She then becomes unable to pay the kitabah installments. The ruling: She becomes umm walad for the first partner who claimed the child. The reasoning is based on the principle that a mukatabah slave cannot be transferred from one ownership to another while the kitabah is in effect (similar to a mudabbarah). Initially, when the first partner claimed his child, his claim is valid because he owns a share in her, and his share becomes umm walad for him. The umm walad status is confined to his share because the kitabah prevents the transfer of ownership between partners. The second partner's claim is also apparently valid because he also owns a share. However, when the slave fails to pay and the kitabah is annulled (as if it never existed), the obstacle to her transfer (i.e., the kitabah contract) is removed. At that point, it becomes clear that she is the umm walad of the first partner entirely, because his intercourse occurred first. This is analogous to the case of a co-owned mudabbarah (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) where if only one partner has a child, the umm walad status is limited to his share. The decisive factor here is the sequence of intercourse and the removal of the kitabah's restriction.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child recognized by her master; she becomes free upon the master's death and cannot be sold.
مدبرة (mudabbarah): A female slave whose manumission is deferred until the master's death (tadbir).
نقل (naql): Transfer of ownership from one person to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the entire slave-girl become umm walad for the first claimant after she fails to pay the kitabah?
A) Because the second claimant's claim becomes invalid
B) Because the kitabah contract is annulled, removing the obstacle to full ownership transfer
C) Because the slave-girl chose the first claimant
D) Because the first claimant paid the kitabah for both partners

Key Takeaway
In a co-owned mukatabah, the first partner to claim a child becomes full owner of her as umm walad if the kitabah is annulled due to her inability to pay.

10 min
Umm Walad of First Co-Owner in Joint Mukataba
Ruling on umm walad status and financial guarantees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on umm walad status for a joint mukataba and explain the financial consequences for each co-owner according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
When a joint mukataba bears children to both co-owners, the first to claim a child secures umm walad status for the entire slave upon contract termination.

This lesson examines a complex scenario of joint ownership and kitaba. The ruling addresses how umm walad status and financial obligations are determined when both co-owners have children with a mukataba slave-girl. The key is the precedence of the first intercourse and the nullification of the kitaba contract upon her inability to pay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the co-owners' intercourse with the joint mukataba and claiming the children. The ruling determines that upon her inability to pay, she becomes umm walad for the first co-owner, and each co-owner has specific financial duties.
The ruling is a legal conclusion, not a prescription of an act.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Qiyas (analogy) to the case of a joint mudabbara. The mukataba is analogized to the mudabbara because both contracts restrict the transfer of ownership.
The analogy is based on the common illa of unable to transfer ownership.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The illa is that the mukataba cannot be transferred from one ownership to another while the kitaba is in effect, similar to a mudabbara. Therefore, the umm walad status is restricted to the share of the claiming co-owner until the obstacle (kitaba) is removed.
When the kitaba ends due to inability, the obstacle is removed, and the umm walad status spreads to the whole slave for the first co-owner.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) differ on whether the second co-owner must guarantee the value of the child. This ikhtilaf will be addressed in the next lesson.
This lesson only covers Abu Hanifa's position.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text declares this as the saying of Abu Hanifa, and it is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school. The authority is Zahir al-Riwayah.
The commentary in Ashraf al-Hidayah confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب
وإذا كانت جارية بين رجلين كاتباها فوطئها أحدهما فجاءت بولد فادعاه ثم وطئها الآخر فجاءت بولد فادعاه ثم عجزت فهي أم ولد الأول؛ لأنه لما ادعى أحدهما الولد صحت دعوته لقيام الملك له فيها، وصار نصيبه أم ولد له؛ لأن المكاتبة لا تقبل النقل من ملك إلى ملك، فيقتصر أمومية الولد على نصيبه كما في المدبرة المشتركة. ولو ادعى الثاني ولدها الأخير صحت دعوته لقيام ملكه ظاهرا. ثم إذا عجزت بعد ذلك جعلت الكتابة كأن لم تكن، وتبين أن الجارية كلها أم ولد للأول؛ لأنه زال المانع من الانتقال، ووطؤه سابق. ويضمن لشريكه نصف قيمتها؛ لأنه تملك نصيبه لما استكمل الاستيلاد. ونصف عقرها لوطئه جارية مشتركة. ويضمن شريكه كمال العقر وقيمة الولد، ويكون ابنه؛ لأنه بمنزلة المغرور؛ لأنه حين وطئها كان ملكه قائما ظاهرا. وولد المغرور ثابت النسب منه حر بالقيمة على ما عرف. لكنه وطئ أم ولد الغير حقيقة فيلزمه كمال العقر. وأيهما دفع العقر إلى المكاتبة جاز؛ لأن الكتابة ما دامت باقية فحق القبض لها لاختصاصها بمنافعها وأبدالها. وإذا عجزت ترد العقر إلى المولى لظهور اختصاصه. وهذا الذي ذكرنا كله قول أبي حنيفة.
The Book of Mukatab: When a slave-girl is shared between two men and they both make her a mukataba, then one of them has intercourse with her and she gives birth to a child and he claims it, then the other has intercourse and she gives birth to a child and he claims it, then she becomes unable (to pay), she becomes umm walad for the first; because when one of them claimed the child, his claim is valid due to his ownership in her being established, and his share becomes umm walad for him; because the mukataba does not accept transfer from one ownership to another, so the umm walad status is restricted to his share, as in the joint mudabbara. And if the second claimed her last child, his claim is valid because his ownership is apparently established. Then when she becomes unable after that, the kitaba is made as if it never existed, and it becomes clear that the entire slave-girl is umm walad for the first; because the obstacle to transfer is removed, and his intercourse was earlier. And he guarantees to his partner half of her value; because he possessed his share when he completed istilad. And half of her 'aqr due to his intercourse with a joint slave-girl. And his partner guarantees the full 'aqr and the value of the child, and the child is his son; because he is in the position of a deceived person (mughrar); because when he had intercourse, his ownership was apparently established. And the child of a deceived person has established lineage from him and is free with payment of value, as is known. But he in reality had intercourse with another's umm walad, so the full 'aqr is obligatory on him. And whichever of them pays the 'aqr to the mukataba is permissible; because as long as the kitaba remains, the right of receipt belongs to her due to her exclusive claim to her benefits and compensation. And when she becomes unable, she returns the 'aqr to the master because his exclusive right becomes apparent. And all of this that we have mentioned is the saying of Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book of Mukatab. The scenario: two men jointly own a female slave and both enter into a kitaba contract with her, making her a mukataba. The first co-owner has intercourse with her, she gives birth to a child, and he claims the child. Then the second co-owner does the same, and she gives birth to another child, and he also claims it. Subsequently, she becomes unable to pay the kitaba installments (ajiz). The ruling: she becomes umm walad (mother of the master's child) for the first co-owner only, not the second. The reasoning: when the first claimed the child, his claim is valid because he had ownership over her at that time (the kitaba does not transfer full ownership immediately). Since the mukataba cannot be transferred from one ownership to another while the kitaba is in effect, the status of umm walad is restricted to his share only, analogously to a joint mudabbara (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death). When the second claims his child, his claim is also valid because his ownership is apparent. However, when she becomes unable to pay, the kitaba contract is nullified, and it is revealed that the entire slave-girl is the umm walad of the first, because the obstacle (the kitaba) that prevented the spread of umm walad status to the whole slave is removed, and his intercourse was earlier. Regarding financial consequences: the first co-owner owes the second half the value of the slave-girl (since he effectively acquired the second's share by completing istilad—full enslavement? Actually, here istilad means begetting a child, which makes the mother umm walad, and since upon nullification of kitaba the first becomes owner of the whole, he must compensate the second for his lost share). He also owes half the 'aqr (customary dower) for having intercourse with a joint slave-girl. The second co-owner owes the full 'aqr and the value of the child, and the child becomes his son (free with payment of value). He is treated like a mughrar (deceived person) because when he had intercourse, his ownership was apparently valid. However, in reality, he had intercourse with another's umm walad (the first's), so he must pay the full 'aqr (dower) for that violation. Whichever of them pays the 'aqr to the mukataba is permissible while the kitaba is in effect, because she has the right to its proceeds. When she becomes unable, she returns it to the master. This entire ruling is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukātaba): A female slave who has entered into a contract of kitaba with her master(s), agreeing to pay a sum for her freedom in installments.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who has borne a child to her master; upon the master's death, she becomes free, and the child is free and inherits.
عقر (ʿaqr): The customary dower or compensation for having intercourse with a slave-girl; in the context of a joint slave, it is divided between co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a joint mukataba who bears children to both co-owners, why does she become the umm walad of the first co-owner and not the second after she becomes unable to pay?
A) Because the first co-owner's intercourse was earlier.
B) Because the second co-owner's claim was invalid.
C) Because the first co-owner's share was larger.
D) Because the second co-owner did not pay the 'aqr.

Key Takeaway
When a joint mukataba bears children to both co-owners and then defaults, the entire slave becomes umm walad for the first co-owner, with specific financial compensations between them.

Objection to Second Co-Owner's Guarantee of Child's Value
Objection and responses regarding child's value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the valuation of a child born to a joint mukataba and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The child of an umm walad may be valuable under one narration of Abu Hanifa, resolving an apparent contradiction in the madhhab.

This passage addresses a subtle objection within the Hanafi school: if an umm walad is valueless, how can her child be valuable? The author of al-Hidayah ruled that the second co-owner must pay the child's value, but an opponent argues from Abu Hanifa's own principle. We will examine two responses, one rejected and one accepted, that reconcile the ruling with the imam's statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the passage and extract the objection: because the umm walad has no value (according to Abu Hanifa), her child should also have no value, so the second co-owner should not guarantee its value.
The objection is based on a qiyas from the mother to the child.
2
Analyze the basis of the objection
Understand the principle behind the objection: the ruling of the child follows the ruling of the mother. If the mother is not compensable, the child is not either.
This is a valid intra-Hanafi deduction.
3
Evaluate the first response
Some scholars claimed that the guarantee of the child's value relies on the opinion of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not Abu Hanifa. But the author of al-'Inaya rejects this because the base text explicitly says it is all the saying of Abu Hanifa.
4
Examine the second response
Al-'Inaya proposes that Abu Hanifa has two narrations regarding the valuation of an umm walad. In one narration, she and her child are considered valuable (qabil li al-taqawwum). The ruling in the matn follows that narration.
This reconciles the apparent contradiction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the child is valuable and the second co-owner must pay its value. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and supported by the second narration.
The first response is rejected as inconsistent with the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: ويضمن شريكه كمال العقر وقيمة الولد پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دوسرا شریک (واطی ثانی) شریک اول کے لئے بچہ کی قیمت کا ضامن نہیں ہونا چاہیے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کے بچہ کا حکم خود ام ولد کا سا ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ام ولد کی کوئی قیمت نہیں تو ایسے ہی اسکے بچہ کی بھی کوئی قیمت نہ ہوگی۔
اس کا جواب بعض نے یہ دیا ہے کہ بچہ کی قیمت کا ضامن ہونا قول صاحبین پر مبنی ہے۔ لیکن بقول صاحب عنایہ یہ جواب کچھ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ جواب "وهذا الذي ذكرناه كله قول أبي حنيفة" کے بالکل منافی ہے۔
صاحب عنایہ نے اس کا دوسرا جواب یہ ذکر کیا ہے کہ ام ولد کے تقوم کی بابت امام ابو حنیفہ سے دو روایتیں ہیں۔ تو ایک روایت کے مطابق بچہ متقوم ہوگا۔ فكان حراج القيمة.
Warning: Concerning 'and his partner guarantees the full 'aqr and the value of the child', an objection arises: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the second partner (the second co-owner) should not be guarantor of the value of the child for the first partner, because the ruling of the child of an umm walad is like that of the umm walad herself, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the umm walad has no value, so likewise her child would have no value. Some have answered that the guarantor of the value of the child depends on the statement of the Sahibayn. But according to the author of al-'Inaya, this answer is nothing, because it entirely contradicts 'and this that we have mentioned is all the saying of Abu Hanifa'. The author of al-'Inaya mentioned another answer: that regarding the valuation of the umm walad, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. According to one narration, the child is valuable, so he would be free with payment of value.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This is a critical refinement addressing an objection raised against the earlier ruling that the second co-owner must guarantee the value of the child. The objection is based on an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, an umm walad (mother of the master's child) has no financial value—she cannot be sold and her value is not assessed. Therefore, her child should likewise have no value, contradicting the requirement for the second co-owner to pay its value. The text presents two responses to this objection. The first response, by some scholars, claims that the guarantee of the child's value is actually based on the opinion of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), not Abu Hanifa. However, the author of al-'Inaya rejects this answer as inconsistent with the text that explicitly says 'this is all the saying of Abu Hanifa'. The second response, favored by al-'Inaya, states that there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the valuation of an umm walad. In one narration, the umm walad and her child are considered valuable (qabil li al-taqawwum), so the child can be appraised and the second co-owner must pay its value. This resolves the apparent contradiction. The passage shows the rigorous internal debate within the Hanafi school and the effort to reconcile differing narrations.

Key Terms
تقوم (taqawwum): Possessing financial value in the eyes of the law; the status of being appraisable and compensable.
مغرور (mughrar): A person who is deceived into thinking a woman is his own when she is actually another's, leading to lineage of the child and obligation of value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first response mentioned in the objection, on which opinion is the guarantee of the child's value based?
A) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone.
B) The opinion of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
C) The opinion of Imam Shafi'i.
D) The opinion of the companion 'Umar.

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction in Abu Hanifa's position is resolved by the existence of two narrations; the relied-upon ruling values the child and requires the second co-owner to pay.

advanced
12 min
Joint Mukatabah Becoming Umm Walad: Sahibayn's Partial Revocation Argument
Intra-Hanafi dispute on joint mukatabah and umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Sahibayn's argument for partially annulling a joint mukatabah's kitabah to complete istilad, distinguish their reasoning from tadbir and sale of mukatab, and state the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Kitabah is revocable to complete umm walad status without harming the slave; unlike tadbir or sale.

In this passage, we delve into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a joint mukatabah (a female slave under a kitabah contract co-owned by two masters). When one co-owner claims a child from her, does she become his umm walad entirely, and what happens to the kitabah and the second co-owner's rights? Imam Abu Hanifa maintains the kitabah remains intact, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the kitabah can be partially annulled to complete the istilad (umm walad status). This lesson unpacks their reasoning, the analogies they distinguish, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Dispute
State the facts: a joint mukatabah, one co-owner claims the child, becomes umm walad for him. The dispute: does the kitabah remain fully intact (Abu Hanifa) or can it be partially annulled to complete the umm walad status (Sahibayn)?
Scenario: two co-owners, one claims paternity, the other later has intercourse.
2
State Each Side's Position
Abu Hanifa: the kitabah remains intact, and the prior rulings on 'aqr (given to the mukatabah, returned upon incapacity) apply. Sahibayn: she becomes wholly the first's umm walad; the kitabah is annulled only to the extent needed without harming the mukatabah.
Sahibayn argue by consensus (ijma') that istilad must be completed if possible.
3
Analyze Sahibayn's Core Argument
They claim kitabah is revocable (qabil li al-faskh), unlike tadbir (irrevocable). The annulment is partial to avoid harming the mukatabah, who retains rights to earnings and kitabah obligations beyond the umm walad status.
They rebut the analogy to tadbir and sale of mukatab.
4
Distinguish from Tadbir and Sale of Mukatab
Tadbir is irrevocable, so a joint mudabbarah cannot be made umm walad by one co-owner after the other. Sale of a mukatab would annul the entire kitabah, harming the slave, unlike partial revocation here.
This distinction shows why kitabah is uniquely suited for partial annulment.
5
Determine Practical Consequences
For the second co-owner: his intercourse does not establish lineage or freedom by value, but no hadd (due to shubhah), and full 'aqr is due. On kitabah payment: some say half, others full. The second co-owner's intercourse is unlawful for establishing lineage but not criminally penalized.
Thamarah al-khilaf: difference in whether lineage/freedom is established and the kitabah payment amount.

Book of Mukatab. The previous discussion about a joint slave woman becoming umm walad: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that she is not liable in case of sale or usurpation because her value is not guaranteed. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: She becomes umm walad for the first claimant, and the second may not have intercourse with her. Because when the first claimed the child, she became entirely his umm walad, as completing umm walad status is necessary by consensus if possible. Here it is possible by annulling the kitabah, since kitabah is revocable. So the kitabah is annulled to the extent that does not harm the mukatabah, and remains beyond that. This is unlike tadbir, which is irrevocable, and unlike sale of mukatab, which would harm the mukatab. When she becomes wholly his umm walad, the second has intercourse with another's umm walad, so lineage is not established, nor does the child become free by value. However, hadd is not required due to shubhah, but full 'aqr is due because intercourse never lacks one of the two penalties. Regarding the kitabah: some say half the kitabah payment is due because the contract is annulled only where no harm occurs; others say full payment is due because the annulment is only for ownership purposes and does not affect the payment. The mukatabah receives the 'aqr due to her right to her earnings. If she becomes incapable and returns to slavery, the 'aqr goes to her master. The commentary clarifies that the Sahibayn's view is that she becomes fully umm walad for the first, so the second's intercourse is unlawful (in terms of establishing lineage, not permissibility itself). The complete umm walad status is achieved by consensus if possible, and here it is possible by annulling the kitabah partially. Unlike tadbir (irrevocable) and unlike sale of mukatab (which would harm the mukatab). The response to the question about tadbir and sale: kitabah is revocable, tadbir is not; sale of mukatab would annul the kitabah entirely, harming the mukatab.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding a joint mukatabah who becomes umm walad for one co-owner. The text first clarifies that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the prior rulings about the 'aqr being given to the mukatabah and its return upon incapacity are established. Then it presents the Sahibayn's view: when one co-owner claims the child from the mukatabah, she becomes fully his umm walad. This is based on the principle that completing istilad (umm walad status) is obligatory by consensus if possible, and here it is possible by annulling the kitabah contract partially—only to the extent that does not harm the mukatabah. The Sahibayn distinguish this from tadbir (a declaration of freedom upon death), which is irrevocable, so the second co-owner cannot make her umm walad in that case. They also distinguish from sale of a mukatab, which would completely annul the kitabah and harm the slave. Consequently, the second co-owner's intercourse does not establish lineage, nor does the child become free by paying value, but hadd is not applied due to shubhah (doubt) arising from the shared ownership and kitabah. The second co-owner must pay the full 'aqr (dower). There is a disagreement among the later scholars: some say only half the kitabah payment is due because the contract is annulled only for the purpose of completing istilad without harming the mukatabah, and the dropping of half payment does not harm her. Others hold the full payment is due because the annulment is limited to ownership rights and does not affect the obligation of the kitabah price. The passage also includes responses to hypothetical objections concerning tadbir and sale of mukatab, emphasizing the unique revocability of kitabah. This detailed analysis serves to clarify the legal positions within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to be freed upon payment of a sum.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master; she becomes free upon the master's death.
عقر ('aqr): The dower or compensation payable for intercourse with a slave woman.
کتابت (kitabah): The contract between a master and slave for the slave's freedom in exchange for payments.
تدبیر (tadbir): A declaration by a master that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
استیلاد (istilad): The process of a female slave becoming umm walad by bearing her master's child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what happens to the kitabah contract when one co-owner claims a child from the joint mukatabah?
A) The kitabah is completely annulled.
B) The kitabah remains entirely in effect.
C) The kitabah is partially annulled to the extent that does not harm the mukatabah.
D) The kitabah is transformed into a tadbir contract.

Key Takeaway
Partial annulment of kitabah is permissible to complete umm walad status because it does not harm the slave, unlike tadbir or sale of a mukatab.

intermediate
6 min
Effect of Istilad on Badal Kitabah for a Mukatabah (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Dispute on whether half or full kitabah compensation is due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the badal kitabah when a mukatabah becomes an umm walad, explain the reasoning of each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a mukatabah becomes an umm walad, the majority of Hanafi scholars hold that full kitabah compensation remains wajib, not half.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya presents a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding the effect of a mukatabah becoming an umm walad (through her master's intercourse) on the kitabah compensation. The central question is whether the compensation is reduced to half or remains full. Understanding the reasoning behind both views and the preferred fatwa position is essential for correctly applying the rulings of kitabah.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the two views: some scholars (Shaikh Zahidi, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi) say half is wajib; the majority of mashayikh say full is wajib.
Remember that both views are within the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the minority's proof
The minority argue that kitabah was opened in a matter without harm, so dropping half does no harm.
This is a dalil of absence of harm.
3
Analyse the majority's proof
The majority argue that kitabah was opened out of necessity for ownership; dropping half would nullify the contract's effect. Also, the master's right is considered.
The principle 'adam al-manh' (lack of obstruction) governs kitabah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the amount the mukatabah must pay: half or full.
This affects the master's financial right.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The author sides with the majority, giving preference to the master's side.
The relied-upon position is full compensation.

A slave-girl became mukatabah, so now according to some, half of the kitabah compensation is obligatory upon her. Because kitabah was opened in a matter in which harm does not occur, and half of the compensation being with her does not cause any harm. Shaikh Zahidi and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi have chosen this. His statement: 'and it is said it is obligatory...' etc. And some, i.e., the general mashayikh, have said that full compensation will be obligatory. Because kitabah was opened only out of necessity due to acquisition of ownership, so in the dropping of half compensation, the effect of the kitabah contract would not appear, and in keeping half compensation, there is consideration for the master (the first umm walad). Although the dropping of compensation does not cause harm to the mukatabah. So the side of the master is given preference because in kitabah the original principle is lack of obstruction. His statement: 'and the mukatabah is the one who...' etc. And the 'aqr (dower) of the mukatabah will be given to her because she is more entitled to compensation for her usufruct, and if she becomes raqiqa (slave) due to inability, then it will be returned to her master, because now the right of her master (the first umm walad) is manifested, as has been stated in the explanation of Abu Hanifa's saying.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a mukatabah becomes an umm walad (mother of a child) due to her master's intercourse. The issue is whether the kitabah compensation is reduced to half or remains full. The author presents two views: some scholars (Shaikh Zahidi, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi) hold that only half the compensation is due, reasoning that the kitabah contract was opened for a purpose where no harm is caused, and having half the compensation with her does not harm. The majority of mashayikh hold that full compensation is due, because the kitabah was opened only out of necessity due to the master's need to acquire ownership, so the contract's effect should be fully preserved; dropping half the compensation would nullify the contract's effect. Additionally, keeping the full compensation shows consideration for the master's right. The passage then addresses the 'aqr (dower or hire) of the mukatabah: it is given to her because she is entitled to compensation for her usufruct. If she becomes a slave again due to inability to pay, the 'aqr is returned to her master (the first umm walad), as the master's right becomes clear.

Key Terms
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The compensation agreed upon in the kitabah contract for the mukatabah's freedom.
عقر ('aqr): The dower or compensation for usufruct of a slave-girl; here it refers to the mukatabah's compensation for her own usufruct.
مکاتبہ (mukatabah): A female slave who has a kitabah contract to earn her freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the ruling on the badal kitabah when a mukatabah becomes an umm walad?
A) The kitabah is void and she becomes free immediately.
B) Half of the badal kitabah is wajib.
C) Full badal kitabah is wajib.
D) The badal kitabah is cancelled and she must pay a different amount.

Key Takeaway
When a mukatabah becomes an umm walad, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is that full kitabah compensation remains wajib, based on the principle of preserving the contract's effect and the master's right.

intermediate
10 min
Guarantee Amount and Tadbir in Joint Mukatabah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guarantee amount and unanimous tadbir voidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish and apply the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the guarantee (daman) for acquiring a partner's share in a joint mukatabah, and explain the unanimous ruling on tadbir validity with its differing rationales.

Core Idea
The guarantee amount for acquiring a partner's share in a mukatabah is wajib, but its calculation differs: value as mukatabah or the lesser of that and remaining compensation.

This lesson examines a case where two partners jointly own a mukatabah slave-girl, and one partner has intercourse, leading to her acquisition through istilad. The first partner must guarantee the second partner's lost share. The Hanafi imams differ on how to value this guarantee. Additionally, if the second partner attempts to declare tadbir, it is void—though the Imāms agree on the result, their reasoning varies. Understanding these nuances is key to applying Hanafi partnership law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two partners jointly own a mukatabah slave-girl. Partner A has intercourse with her, leading to istilad (acquisition of ownership). Partner B does not have intercourse but may have made her mudabbarah. The slave-girl later becomes unable to pay the kitabah compensation.
The scenario assumes the slave-girl was a mukatabah at the time of intercourse.
2
State the guarantee obligation and its basis
Partner A must guarantee Partner B for acquiring his share. This is daman al-tamalluk (guarantee of ownership), which is wajib regardless of the guarantor's wealth. The amount is disputed.
Daman al-tamalluk is distinct from contractual guarantees; it is unaffected by financial status.
3
Distinguish the two opinions on guarantee amount
Abu Yusuf: guarantee half the value of the slave-girl as a mukatabah. Reasoning: Partner A acquired the share while she was a mukatabah, so her value is calculated accordingly. Imam Muhammad: guarantee the lesser of half her value as a mukatabah and half the remaining kitabah compensation. Reasoning: Partner B's right could be in the slave-girl herself (if she becomes unable) or in the compensation (if she pays), so the lesser is certain.
Both opinions are valid within the Hanafi school; the text does not prefer one.
4
Analyze the tadbir case
If Partner B declares tadbir on the slave-girl before her inability, but she then becomes unable, the tadbir is void. All Hanafi imams agree, but reasons differ: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say Partner A already owned her via istilad before the inability, so tadbir was on non-owned property. Abu Hanifa says inability retroactively proves Partner A owned his share from the time of intercourse, so tadbir was on another's property.
Despite different reasoning, the ruling is unanimous: tadbir is void.
5
Apply the final rulings
The slave-girl becomes umm walad for Partner A. Partner A must pay Partner B half the 'aqr (compensation for intercourse) and half her value (as a mukatabah). The child belongs to Partner A. These conclusions are unanimous.
The guarantee amount follows either Abu Yusuf or Muhammad; no single mufta bihi is given.
