He said: The first partner guarantees to his partner, in analogy to Abu Yusuf's statement, half of her value as a mukatabah, because he acquired his partner's share while she was a mukatabah, so he guarantees it whether he is wealthy or poor because it is a guarantee of ownership. And in Muhammad's statement, he guarantees the lesser of half her value and half of what remains of the kitabah compensation, because his partner's right is in half of the slave-girl (on the basis of inability) and in half of the compensation (on the basis of payment), so due to uncertainty between them, the lesser is obligatory... Translation: The first partner guarantees to his partner, in analogy to Abu Yusuf's statement, half the value of the slave-girl as a mukatabah, because he became owner of his partner's share while she was a mukatabah, so he guarantees it whether he is wealthy or poor because it is a guarantee of ownership. And in Imam Muhammad's statement, he guarantees the lesser of half her value and half of the remaining kitabah compensation, because his partner's right is in half of the slave-girl on account of inability, and in half of the compensation on account of payment, so due to uncertainty between them, the lesser of them is obligatory... Explanation: Then the first partner guarantees to his partner, by analogy to the aforementioned statement of Abu Yusuf, half the value of the slave-girl calculated as a mukatabah. Thus, if a slave is jointly owned by two partners as a mukatab, and one partner frees him, then in that case of freeing, according to Abu Yusuf, half of the slave's value as a mukatab is obligatory. So in our case of istilad, the analogy to Abu Yusuf's statement is that here too, the first coitus-provider should guarantee half the value of the slave-girl as a mukatabah to his partner, because he acquired his partner's share when she was a mukatabah, so he guarantees the value of that share, whether he is wealthy or poor, because it is a guarantee of ownership, evidenced by the fact that manifestations of ownership like permissibility of intercourse and employment have become apparent, and a guarantee of ownership is not affected by wealth or poverty. His statement: 'and in Muhammad's statement...' etc. And in Imam Muhammad's statement, he guarantees the lesser of half her value and half of the remaining kitabah compensation, because the partner's right is attached to two considerations: if the mukatab becomes unable to pay the compensation, then his right is in half the slave-girl; and if he pays the compensation, then his right is in half the compensation. So because the partner's right is ambiguous between the two considerations, the lesser is obligatory, since what is lesser is certain. Then the second (partner) did not have intercourse with her, but made her mudabbarah, then she became unable, so the tadbir becomes void. He said: If the second did not have intercourse with her but made her mudabbarah, then she became unable, the tadbir becomes void because it did not coincide with ownership. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent, because the istilad-maker owned her before her inability. According to Abu Hanifa, because by inability it becomes clear that he had owned his share from the time of intercourse, so it becomes clear that the tadbir coincided with the property of another, while tadbir depends on ownership, unlike lineage because it depends on deception (ghurur) as previously stated. He said: She is an umm walad for the first (partner), because he acquired his partner's share and istilad is complete as we explained, and he guarantees to his partner half of her 'aqr due to his intercourse with a shared slave-girl, and half of her value, because he acquired half of her by istilad, which is acquisition by value, and the child belongs to the first (partner) because his claim of lineage is valid due to the presence of a rectifying factor, and this is the statement of all of them, and its reason is what we explained. Translation: And if the second did not have intercourse with her but made her mudabbarah, then she became unable, the tadbir becomes void, because it did not coincide with ownership. According to the Sahibayn, it is apparent, because the one who made her umm walad owned her before her inability. According to Abu Hanifa, because from inability it is revealed that he owned his share from the time of intercourse, so it becomes clear that the tadbir coincided with the property of another, while tadbir depends on ownership, unlike lineage which depends on deception. And the slave-girl will be an umm walad for the first claimant, because he became owner of his partner's share and istilad is complete. And he guarantees to his partner half of her 'aqr for his intercourse with the shared slave-girl, and half of her value, because he became owner of half of her by istilad, and this ownership is by value. And the child belongs to the first claimant because his claim of lineage is valid due to the presence of a rectifying factor, and this is the statement of all of them. Explanation: If the second partner did not have intercourse with the aforementioned mukatabah but made her mudabbarah, then she became unable to pay the compensation, then the tadbir will be void, because it did not coincide with ownership. According to the Sahibayn, it is apparent, because the partner who made her umm walad had already owned her before her inability, so the kitabah was rescinded before the tadbir, hence the tadbir is not valid. According to Abu Hanifa, because from the slave-girl's inability it becomes clear that the first coitus-provider had owned the second partner's share from the time he had intercourse, so the second partner's making her mudabbarah coincided with the ownership of another, while tadbir is valid only when there is ownership; without ownership, tadbir is not valid. As for lineage, it can be valid without ownership, meaning if deception occurs, then deception...
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario of a jointly-owned mukatabah where the first partner (first claimant of umm walad) has intercourse, and the second partner either does nothing or makes her mudabbarah. The text first discusses the guarantee (daman) owed by the first partner to the second partner for acquiring his share through istilad. According to analogical reasoning from Abu Yusuf's position, the first partner guarantees half the value of the slave-girl as a mukatabah, regardless of his financial status, because it is a guarantee of ownership (daman tamalluk) which is unaffected by wealth or poverty. According to Imam Muhammad, he guarantees the lesser of half the value and half the remaining kitabah compensation, because the second partner's right is ambiguous: if the mukatabah becomes unable, his right is in the slave-girl herself; if she pays, his right is in half the compensation. The lesser amount is certain and thus obligatory. The text then discusses the case where the second partner does not have intercourse but makes her mudabbarah. Both Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Abu Hanifa agree that the tadbir is void, but for different reasons: according to the Sahibayn, the first partner already owned her through istilad before her inability, so the tadbir was made on a non-owned slave. According to Abu Hanifa, the inability retroactively proves that the first partner owned his share from the time of intercourse, so the tadbir was made on another's property. Finally, the text concludes that the slave-girl is an umm walad for the first partner, who must pay half her 'aqr (due to intercourse) and half her value (due to istilad), and the child belongs to him. All imams agree on this final ruling.

Key Terms
ضمان تملک (daman al-tamalluk): A guarantee that arises from acquiring ownership of another's share in a property; it is not affected by the guaranteeor's financial status.
تدبیر (tadbir): The act of a master declaring a slave to be free upon his death; requires ownership at the time of declaration.
عقر ('aqr): The fixed compensation paid by a man who has intercourse with a slave-girl; here half the 'aqr is due from the first partner for intercourse with the jointly-owned mukatabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what amount does the first partner guarantee to the second partner for acquiring his share of the mukatabah?
A) Half the market value of the slave-girl as an ordinary slave.
B) Half the value as a mukatabah.
C) The full remaining kitabah compensation.
D) The lesser of half the mukatabah value and half the remaining kitabah compensation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes two valid opinions on the guarantee amount for joint mukatabah, and tadbir by a non-owner is void regardless of the reasoning.

Recovery After Freeing a Co-Owned Mukataba Who Fails
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recovery after freeing a mukataba co-owned slave who then fails

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the recovery of compensation from a co-owned mukataba freed by one partner who then becomes 'ajiz, and explain the underlying principle of tajazzi al-'itq.

Core Idea
Emancipation divisibility determines whether a co-owner can recover from the slave after failure.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a jointly owned mukataba (female slave under a kitaba contract). When one co-owner frees her and she later fails to pay the kitaba price, can the freeing partner recover from her the compensation he paid to the other co-owner? The answer hinges on whether emancipation is divisible (tajazzi al-'itq) or indivisible—a key doctrinal difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Two co-owners jointly make their female slave a mukataba. One partner frees her while he is wealthy. Later, she becomes unable to pay the kitaba (she becomes 'ajiz).
The scenario assumes the freeing partner was financially capable at the time of freeing.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and his reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that the freeing partner must pay half the slave's value to the other co-owner, but then he can recover that amount from the slave. His reasoning: emancipation is divisible; the freer only freed his own share, leaving the other's share as a mukataba. When she becomes 'ajiz, the freer's share reverts to slavery, so he can claim against her.
The principle of tajazzi al-'itq underlies this view.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and their reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the freeing partner cannot recover from the slave. They argue emancipation is indivisible; once one partner frees, the entire slave becomes free. When she fails, she reverts to full slavery as if she were never a mukataba, so no recovery is possible.
For the Sahibayn, the whole slave is affected by the act of freeing.
4
Trace the dispute to the broader implications
The difference extends to three matters: recourse (ruju'), options (khiyarat) for the silent partner, and patronage (wala'). The commentary explains that the root is the position on divisibility of emancipation.
Before 'ajz, the silent partner's rights also differ according to each view.

قوله فاما قبل العجز الخ - مذکورہ تفصیل تو باندی کے عاجز ہونے کے بعد سے متعلق ہے۔ رہا اس کے عاجز ہونے سے پہلے کا حکم سو اس کے عاجز ہونے سے پہلے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شریک کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ آزاد کنندہ سے تاوان لے لے۔ اس لیے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جب اعتاق متجری ہے۔ یعنی اس کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں تو آزاد کرنے کا اثر یہی ہے کہ دوسرے شریک کا حصہ مثل مکاتب کے ہو جائے اور چونکہ وہ مکاتب موجود ہے تو اس کے فعل سے دوسرے کے حصہ میں کوئی ضر ر نہیں پہنچا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس سے پہلے ہی سے مکاتبہ ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتاق چونکہ متجری نہیں ہے تو اس کے آزاد کرنے سے کل آزاد ہو جائے گی تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنے حصہ کی قیمت بحساب مکاتب ہونے کے تاوان لے لے بشرطیکہ آزاد کننده خوشحال ہو ۔ اگر تنگدست ہو تو مملوک اس قیمت کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ ضمان اعتاق ہے تو تنگدستی و خوشحالی سے مختلف ہوگا۔
If both co-owners made her a mukataba, then one of them freed her while he is wealthy, then she became unable (to pay), then the freer guarantees to his partner half her value and recovers that from her according to Abu Hanifa. They (Sahibayn) said: He does not recover from her because when she became unable and was returned to slavery, she becomes as if she never ceased to be a slave. The answer in this is based on the difference regarding recourse, options, etc., as it is the issue of divisibility of emancipation which we have established in the chapter of emancipation. As for before inability, he does not have the right to make the freer liable according to Abu Hanifa, because when emancipation is divisible in his view, its effect is to make the share of the non-freer like a mukatab, so his partner's share is not changed because she was a mukataba before. According to them (Sahibayn), since it is not divisible, the whole becomes free, so he can make him liable for the value of his share as a mukatab if he is wealthy, and the slave will be required to earn (ista'sa) if he is poor, because it is a guarantee of emancipation, so it differs. The Urdu commentary explains the above and elaborates on the three matters: recourse (ruju'), options (khiyarat), and patronage (wala') derived from the same principle. Before 'ajz, Abu Hanifa denies the partner the right to demand guarantee because his share remains as a mukatab; Sahibayn grant him that right because the whole became free.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah discusses a specific scenario in the chapter of mukatab. Two co-owners jointly make their female slave a mukataba, meaning she contracts to earn her freedom by paying a sum. One partner then sets her free while he is financially capable. Later, she becomes unable to pay the kitaba (aajiz). The ruling concerns whether the freeing partner must compensate his co-owner and whether he can then recover that from the slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the freeing partner must pay half the slave's value to the other partner, but then he can recover that amount from the slave herself. The reasoning is that according to Abu Hanifa, emancipation is divisible (tajazzi al-'itq): one co-owner can free his share, and the other's share remains as it is. Here, the other share remained a mukataba, so when she fails, his share reverts to slavery, allowing the freer to claim against her. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that emancipation is indivisible; once one partner frees, the entire slave becomes free. Thus, when she fails, she reverts to full slavery as if she were originally a slave, so no recovery is possible from her. The passage then relates this ikhtilaf to the broader principles of recourse (ruju'), options (khiyarat), and patronage (wala') in cases of co-ownership. Before the slave's inability, Abu Hanifa says the other partner cannot demand compensation because his share remains effectively a mukataba, so no loss; the Sahibayn say he can because the freer's act freed the whole, damaging his share. The commentary from Ashraf al-Hidaya elaborates on these three matters and confirms that the root cause is the position on divisibility of emancipation.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitaba) with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
تجزى الاعتاق (tajazzi al-'itq): The principle that emancipation is divisible; a co-owner can free his share, and the other share remains unfree.
عجز ('ajz): Inability to pay the kitaba; if the mukatab fails to pay, he reverts to full slavery.
ولاء (wala'): Patronage right that attaches to the emancipator; it gives him inheritance rights from the freed slave.
سعاية (sa'aya): The requirement of the slave to work and earn to pay the kitaba price to the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, after a co-owned mukataba is freed by one partner and then becomes 'ajiz, what is the ruling on the freeing partner's right to recover the compensation from the slave?
A) He cannot recover because the slave reverts to full slavery.
B) He can recover because emancipation is divisible and his share reverted to slavery.
C) He can recover only if the other partner agrees.
D) He can recover but only after the slave becomes free again.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of emancipation (tajazzi al-'itq) is the key principle that determines whether a co-owner can recover from a slave after freeing and subsequent failure to pay kitaba.

intermediate

The Shared Mukatab and Divisibility of I'taq: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains ruling on shared mukatab freed by one partner and general options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on divisibility of i'taq and explain how it determines the silent partner's three options in a shared mukatab case.

Core Idea
I'taq can be partial according to Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn say it is indivisible — the root of all differences in shared manumission.

This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a shared slave-girl who is a mukatabah (contracting for freedom). One partner frees his share, but the slave later becomes unable to pay. At stake are three issues: whether the freeing partner can recover compensation from the slave, what options the silent partner has, and who acquires wala' (patronage). All three hinge on a single usul question: Is the act of freeing (i'taq) divisible into parts?

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the three sub-issues
The scenario: two partners jointly own a slave-girl who is a mukatabah. One partner frees his half. The slave then becomes unable to pay the kitabah. Three issues arise: (1) Can the freeing partner recover from the slave? (2) What options does the silent partner have? (3) Who gets wala'?
The same issues also arise in the case of a shared non-mukatab slave (ghair mukatab).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that i'taq is divisible (mutajazzī). Therefore, freeing half is valid and initially does not harm the silent partner's share. When the slave becomes unable, the silent partner has three options unconditionally: free his share, seek sa'yah, or take compensation. If he chooses compensation, the freeing partner may recover from the slave.
Abu Hanifa's principle of tajazzu' allows partial manumission to have legal effect.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its basis
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that i'taq is indivisible. Freeing half effectively frees the entire slave at once. Therefore, the freeing partner cannot recover from the slave. The silent partner's options are conditional: if the freeing partner is wealthy, he can only take compensation; if poor, he can only seek sa'yah. Wala' in all cases goes to the freeing partner.
They rely on the hadith that a manumitter with enough wealth must fully free the slave.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequences)
Under Abu Hanifa: the silent partner has three options always; if he takes compensation, the freeing partner can recover from the slave. Under Sahibayn: options depend on the freeing partner's wealth; the freeing partner never recovers from the slave. Also, wala' is shared under Abu Hanifa if the silent partner frees his share or seeks sa'yah; under Sahibayn, wala' always belongs to the freeing partner.
These differences affect real cases of joint ownership and manumission.
5
Note the mufta bihi (operative position)
In later Hanafi fatwa practice, the view of the Sahibayn is often relied upon, though Abu Hanifa's view remains authoritative. The text of Al-Hidayah presents both without explicit tarjih. For practical fatwa, the wealth-conditioned options of the Sahibayn are generally applied.
Muftis should be aware of both views and choose based on circumstances.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ آزاد کنندہ مالدار ہے۔ پھر باندی بدل کتابت سے عاجز ہوگئی۔ تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک آزاد کنندہ اپنے شریک کو باندی کی نصف قیمت دے کر باندی سے وصول کر لیگا ۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ باندی سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ جب وہ عاجز نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے رقیق کر دی گئی تو گویا وہ برابر رقیق ہی تھی۔ اور غلام مشترک کو ایک شریک کے آزاد کرنے کی صورت میں رجوع و عدم رجوع کی بابت اختلاف ہے کہ اگر ایک شریک آزاد کر دے اور شریک ساکت اس سے ضمان لے لے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک معتق اس غلام سے واپس لے گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وہ غلام سے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ نیز خیارات ثلاثہ کی بابت بھی اختلاف ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک شریک ساکت کو تین اختیارات ہوں گے۔ چاہے اپنے حصہ کو آزاد کر دے چاہے مملوک سے سعایت کرالے۔ چاہے معتق سے تاوان لے لے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک معتق اگر خوشحال ہو تو شریک ساکت اس سے صرف تاوان لے گا۔ اور اگر وہ تنگدست ہو تو صرف غلام سے سعایت کرائے گا۔ اسی طرح ولاء کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اگر شریک ساکت نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا یا غلام سے سعایت کرائی تو اس کی ولاء دونوں شریکوں میں مشترک ہوگی اور اگر اس نے معتق سے تاوان کیا تو ولا معتق کیلئے ہو گی ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ولاء بہر صورت معتق کیلئے ہوگی۔ بہر کیف امور ثلاثہ ( رجوع، خیارات ، ولاء ) میں مذکورہ اختلاف اعتاق کے متجری ہونے اور نہ ہونے کے اختلاف پر مبنی ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اعتاق چونکہ متجزئ ہے اس لئے زیر بحث مسئلہ میں نصف حصہ کو آزاد کر نا صحیح ہوا اور اس کی وجہ سے باندی کے عاجز ہونے سے دوسرے شریک کے حصہ میں کوئی فساد نہیں آیا لیکن جب وہ عاجز ہو گئی تو اب اس کے حصہ میں فساد ظاہر ہو گیا اور ایسی صورت میں شریک ثانی کیلئے تین اختیارات ہیں جب کہ وہ مالدار ہو۔ ایک یہ کہ اپنے حصہ کو آزاد کر دے، دوم یہ کہ مملوک سے سعایت کرالے، سوم یہ کہ معتق سے تاوان لے لے اور اس نے تاوان لینا اختیار کیا ہے۔ تو معتق تاوان دے کر باندی سے وصول کرے گا۔
قوله فاما قبل العجز الخ - مذکورہ تفصیل تو باندی کے عاجز ہونے کے بعد سے متعلق ہے۔ رہا اس کے عاجز ہونے سے پہلے کا حکم سو اس کے عاجز ہونے سے پہلے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شریک کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ آزاد کنندہ سے تاوان لے لے۔ اس لیے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک جب اعتاق متجری ہے۔ یعنی اس کے ٹکڑے ہو سکتے ہیں تو آزاد کرنے کا اثر یہی ہے کہ دوسرے شریک کا حصہ مثل مکاتب کے ہو جائے اور چونکہ وہ مکاتب موجود ہے تو اس کے فعل سے دوسرے کے حصہ میں کوئی ضرر نہیں پہنچا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس سے پہلے ہی سے مکاتبہ ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتاق چونکہ متجری نہیں ہے تو اس کے آزاد کرنے سے کل آزاد ہو جائے گی تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنے حصہ کی قیمت بحساب مکاتب ہونے کے تاوان لے لے بشرطیکہ آزاد کننده خوشحال ہو ۔ اگر تنگدست ہو تو مملوک اس قیمت کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ ضمان اعتاق ہے تو تنگدستی و خوشحالی سے مختلف ہوگا۔
Page 182: Book of the Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 12. The freeing person is wealthy. Then the slave-girl became unable to pay the kitabah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the freeing person will give half the price of the slave-girl to his partner and then recover from the slave-girl. The Sahibayn say: he cannot recover from the slave-girl, because when she was made a slave due to inability, it is as if she was a slave from the beginning. Regarding a shared slave when one partner frees him, there is a dispute concerning revocation or no revocation: if one partner frees and the silent partner takes a guarantee from him, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the manumitter will recover from this slave, but according to the Sahibayn he cannot recover from the slave. Also regarding the three options there is a dispute: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the silent partner will have three options: either free his own share, or seek sa'yah (earning) from the slave, or take compensation from the manumitter. According to the Sahibayn, if the manumitter is wealthy, the silent partner will only take compensation from him; if the manumitter is poor, he will only seek sa'yah from the slave. Similarly, regarding wala' there is a dispute: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the silent partner frees his share or seeks sa'yah from the slave, then the wala' will be shared between both partners; if he takes compensation from the manumitter, then wala' is for the manumitter. According to the Sahibayn, in all cases wala' is for the manumitter. In short, the aforementioned dispute in the three matters (revocation, options, wala') is based on the dispute regarding whether i'taq (manumission) is divisible or not. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since i'taq is divisible, therefore in the issue under discussion, freeing half the share was valid, and due to that, the slave-girl's inability did not cause any corruption in the other partner's share. But when she became unable, then now corruption appears in his share, and in such a situation, the second partner has three options when the manumitter is wealthy: first, free his own share; second, seek sa'yah from the slave; third, take compensation from the manumitter. And he has chosen to take compensation, so the manumitter will pay compensation and then recover from the slave-girl. His saying: 'As for before inability, etc.' - The aforementioned detail pertains to after the slave-girl's inability. As for the ruling before her inability: before her inability, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the partner does not have the option to take compensation from the freeing person, because according to Imam Abu Hanifa, since i'taq is divisible, the effect of freeing is that the other partner's share becomes like a mukatab, and since that mukatab is present, no harm is caused to the other's share by his action, because she was already a mukatabah. According to the Sahibayn, since i'taq is not divisible, then by his freeing, the whole becomes free, so he has the option to take compensation for the price of his share as per being a mukatab, provided the freeing person is wealthy. If he is poor, the slave will perform sa'yah for that price, because this is daman al-i'taq, so it differs with poverty and wealth.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a shared slave-girl (bāndī) who is a mukatabah (a slave who has contracted to earn her freedom by paying her owner). One of the two partners frees his share, but then the slave-girl becomes unable to pay the kitabah (contract). The question is whether the freeing partner can recover from her the amount he paid to his partner. Imam Abu Hanifa says yes: since i'taq (manumission) is divisible (mutajazzī) in his view, the freeing of half was valid and did not affect the other partner's share initially. But when she became unable, that share became corrupt, so the silent partner has three options: free his share, seek sa'yah from the slave, or take compensation from the freeing partner. Since he chose compensation, the freeing partner pays it and then recovers from the slave-girl. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they hold that i'taq is not divisible, so the freeing of half frees the whole slave. Therefore, the freeing partner cannot recover from her; instead, the silent partner's options depend on the freeing partner's wealth. The dispute extends to three matters: rujū' (whether the freeing partner can recover from the slave), khayārāt (the options of the silent partner), and walā' (patronage rights). The root of all differences is the divisibility of i'taq. The passage then clarifies the ruling before the slave's inability: according to Abu Hanifa, since i'taq is divisible and the slave is still a mukatabah, the silent partner cannot take compensation because no harm has occurred; the slave remains obligated. According to the Sahibayn, since i'taq is indivisible, the entire slave becomes free at once, so the silent partner may take compensation from the freeing partner if he is wealthy, or seek sa'yah from the slave if poor. The commentary follows the author's order, first stating the post-inability ruling, then the pre-inability ruling.

Key Terms
ایقاع (i'taq): The act of manumission or freeing a slave.
تجزئ (tajazzu'): Divisibility - the legal concept that an act can be divided into parts, each having independent effect.
خیارات ثلاثہ (khayārāt thalātha): The three options available to the silent partner when one partner frees a shared slave: free his own share, seek sa'yah from the slave, or take compensation from the freeing partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when one partner frees his share in a shared slave, how many options does the silent partner have if the freeing partner is wealthy?
A) One option: take compensation only
B) Two options: take compensation or seek sa'yah
C) Three options: free his share, seek sa'yah, or take compensation
D) None; the slave becomes automatically free

Key Takeaway
The divergence in the silent partner's options and the freeing partner's right of recovery in a shared mukatab case stems from the foundational question of whether i'taq can be divided (tajazzu'), with Abu Hanifa affirming divisibility and the Sahibayn denying it.

Ruling on Tadbir Preceding I'taq in a Shared Slave
Explains Abu Hanifa's ruling on mudabbar options and the intra-Hanafi dispute over tadbir divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on the options available to a mudabbar-maker when tadbir precedes or follows i'taq, and distinguish the Sahibayn's disagreement regarding the divisibility of tadbir.

Core Idea
If tadbir precedes i'taq, the mudabbar-maker can seek compensation; if i'taq precedes, he cannot – all hinges on the divisibility of tadbir.

In this lesson, we examine a case from Al-Hidayah where two partners own a slave, and one declares a tadbir while the other immediately frees the slave. The order of these actions determines the options available to the mudabbar-maker. Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling is based on the principle that tadbir is divisible (tajazzu'), a point of intra-Hanafi disagreement with the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two sequences: (a) tadbir first, then i'taq; (b) i'taq first, then tadbir. Note the different outcomes.
2
Determine the options in the first scenario
When tadbir precedes i'taq, the mudabbar-maker has three options: liberate his share, seek sa'yah, or claim compensation from the manumitter.
3
Determine the options in the second scenario
When i'taq precedes tadbir, the mudabbar-maker has only two options: liberate his share or seek sa'yah; he cannot claim compensation.
4
Extract the legal cause (illah)
Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that tadbir is divisible (mutajazzī). Thus, a partial tadbir only affects the declarer's share but corrupts the other's share when combined with i'taq, granting options.
This is a point of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf; the Sahibayn hold tadbir is indivisible.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, compensation is possible; under the Sahibayn, it is not because the mudabbar's action is voided.

Page 183: Book of the Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 12. If a slave is shared between two men, one makes him mudabbar (declares that he will be free upon his death), then the other frees him and he is wealthy, then the one who made him mudabbar may either hold the manumitter liable for half the value as a mudabbar, or he may seek sa'yah from the slave, or he may free him. If one frees him and then the other makes him mudabbar, then he cannot hold the manumitter liable; he may seek sa'yah from the slave or free him. Arabic text: "He said: If a slave is between two men, one of them makes him mudabbar, then the other frees him and he is wealthy, then if the one who made him mudabbar wishes, he can hold the manumitter liable for half his value as a mudabbar; if he wishes, he can seek sa'yah from the slave; if he wishes, he can free him. And if one of them frees him and then the other makes him mudabbar, he does not have the option to hold the manumitter liable; he may seek sa'yah from the slave or free him. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and its reason is that tadbir is divisible in his view. So the tadbir of one is confined to his share, but it corrupts the share of the other, so the mudabbar-maker has the choice of freeing, holding liable, and seeking sa'yah, according to his madhhab. When he frees, he no longer has the option of holding liable and seeking sa'yah. His freeing is confined to his share because it is divisible in his view, but it corrupts the share of his partner, so he has the option to hold him liable for the value of his share, and he also has the option of freeing and seeking sa'yah, according to his madhhab. And he holds him liable for the value of his share as a mudabbar because the freeing encountered a mudabbar." Urdu translation: If a slave is shared between two persons, one of them makes him mudabbar, then the other frees him and he is wealthy, then the one who made him mudabbar may either take compensation from the manumitter for half the value as a mudabbar, or seek sa'yah from the slave, or free him. If one freed him and then the other made him mudabbar, the mudabbar-maker will not have the option to take compensation from the manumitter; rather, he will seek sa'yah from the slave or free him. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and its reason is that tadbir is divisible in his view, so one's making mudabbar is confined to his share, but it corrupts the other's share. Thus he will have the option to free, take compensation, and seek sa'yah, as per Imam's madhhab. When he frees, he no longer has the option to take compensation and seek sa'yah, and his freeing is confined to his share because tadbir is divisible in his view, but it corrupts his partner's share. Therefore, he has the option to take compensation for the value of his share, and he also has the option to free and seek sa'yah, as per Imam's madhhab. And he will take compensation for the value of his share as a mudabbar because the freeing has attached to a mudabbar. Explanation of the saying: 'If the slave is between two men, etc.' - A slave was shared between two men, one of them made his share mudabbar, then the other freed his share, and the freeing person is wealthy. Then the mudabbar-maker has three options: either take compensation from the freeing person for half the value as a mudabbar, because the manumitter's freeing corrupted his share; or free his own share; or seek sa'yah from the slave. If one of the partners freed first and then the other made mudabbar, then the mudabbar-maker will only have two options: either free his own share or seek sa'yah from the slave. He cannot take compensation from the manumitter. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the reason is that tadbir is divisible in his view, so one partner's tadbir is confined to his share, but since this tadbir corrupted the other's share (lidhab bab).
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding a shared slave where one partner performs tadbir (declaring the slave free upon his death) and the other performs i'taq (immediate freeing). The order matters. If tadbir comes first, then i'taq, the mudabbar-maker (the one who declared tadbir) has three options because his tadbir is divisible (mutajazzī) in Abu Hanifa's view. Since his tadbir corrupted the other partner's share (who then freed the whole slave), he can choose to: 1) take compensation from the manumitter for half the slave's value as a mudabbar; 2) seek sa'yah from the slave; or 3) free his own share. If he chooses to free, the options of compensation and sa'yah fall away. If i'taq comes first, then tadbir, the mudabbar-maker has only two options (free his share or seek sa'yah), and cannot take compensation from the manumitter. The reason is that when i'taq occurs first, the slave becomes free entirely, so the subsequent tadbir has no effect on the other's share; the mudabbar-maker's tadbir only affects his own share, which is already free? Actually, the reasoning: if i'taq precedes, the slave is already free, so the tadbir is invalid? The text says the mudabbar-maker cannot take compensation because the i'taq already freed the slave, so there is no corruption from the tadbir? The passage is slightly cut off at the end. The commentary explains that Abu Hanifa's view is based on the divisibility of tadbir (tajazzu' al-tadbir), allowing partial ownership effects. The Sahibayn likely disagree, but their view is not detailed here. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute (only Abu Hanifa's view is given, but it implies disagreement). The commentary follows the matn and then provides an Urdu translation and further explanation (tashrīh). It is a ruling with proof (dalil aqli of tajazzu') and talil (identifying the illa of divisibility).

Key Terms
تدبیر (tadbir): A declaration by a master that a slave will be free upon the master's death (mudabbar).
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been declared free upon his master's death.
سعایة (sa'yah): Earning or seeking money by the slave to compensate his owner for his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one partner makes a shared slave mudabbar and then the other partner frees the slave, what options does the mudabbar-maker have?
A) Only one option: free his share
B) Two options: free his share or seek sa'yah
C) Three options: free his share, seek sa'yah, or take compensation from the manumitter
D) No options; the slave is fully free

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of tadbir (tajazzu') is the key principle determining the mudabbar-maker's options, especially the availability of compensation.

intermediate
12 min
Rulings on a Shared Slave: Divisible vs Indivisible – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divisibility of tadbir and itq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options of the mudabbar partner under Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain how the divisibility of tadbir and itq affects those options.

Core Idea
Divisibility of tadbir and itq determines whether a partner can claim compensation, free his share, or have the slave earn.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when two men jointly own a slave, and one makes him mudabbar while the other frees him, what are the legal consequences? The key question is whether the acts of tadbir (promising freedom after death) and itq (immediate freeing) are divisible, meaning they apply only to the doer's share, or indivisible, meaning they affect the entire slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds they are divisible, granting the mudabbar partner options to protect his interest. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), disagree, ruling that such acts are indivisible, leading to different outcomes. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi approach to property rights and contractual effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the parties
Note that the slave is shared equally between two owners. One creates a tadbir (making the slave mudabbar – freeing after death), and the other immediately frees his share. The manumitter is wealthy. Determine who acts first?
Two orders are considered: tadbir first then itq, and itq first then tadbir.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling for each order
Under Abu Hanifa, tadbir and itq are divisible. If tadbir comes first, the mudabbar partner has three options: claim half the mudabbar's value from the manumitter, free his own share, or have the slave earn his share. If itq comes first, the mudabbar partner loses the compensation option and can only free his share or have the slave earn.
The compensation is for half the value of the slave as a mudabbar, not as a mere slave.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling for each order
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, tadbir and itq are indivisible. If tadbir comes first, the later itq is void; the mudabbar partner becomes owner of the entire slave and must pay half his value as a mere slave (not mudabbar), regardless of the manumitter's wealth. If itq comes first, the slave is completely free, so later tadbir is void; the second partner guarantees half the slave's value only if the manumitter is wealthy, otherwise the slave earns it.
Under Sahibayn, the mudabbar partner cannot free his share or have the slave earn; the outcome is a forced transfer or compensation.
4
Identify the key difference: divisibility
Abu Hanifa views tadbir and itq as divisible (tajazzi), meaning they apply only to the doer's share but spoil the other's share, giving options. The Sahibayn view them as indivisible, so one partner's action either transfers ownership or voids the other's action entirely.
The illa (effective cause) for divisibility is that ownership can be partial, and contracts like tadbir and itq can be partially executed.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the mudabbar partner retains flexibility (compensation, freeing, or earning). Under Sahibayn, the outcome is more rigid: either forced ownership or voidance, with compensation dependent on wealth status. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's view.
The difference affects whether the slave can be freed immediately or must earn his freedom, and whether compensation is based on mudabbar value or mere slave value.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
ایک غلام دو آدمیوں میں مشترک ہو ایک نے اسے مدبر بنایا دوسرے نے آزاد کر دیا اور وہ خوش حال ہے جس نے مدبر بنایا چاہے تو معتق کو نصف قیمت مد بر کا ضامن ٹھہرائے اور اگر چاہے غلام سے سعی کرائے اگر چاہے تو آزاد کر دے اگر ایک نے آزاد کیا دوسرے نے مدبر بنایا تو یہ معتق کو ضامن نہیں ٹھہراسکتا غلام سے سعی کرائے یا آزاد کرے
قال وان كان العبد بين رجلين دبره احدهما ثم اعتقه الآخر وهو موسر فان شاء الذي دبره ضمن المعتق نصف قیمته مدبرا وان شاء استسعى العبد وان شاء اعتق وان اعتقه احدهما ثم دبره الآخر لم يكن له ان يضمن المعتق ويستسعى العبد أو يعتق وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ووجهه ان التدبير يتجزى عنده فتدبير احدهما يقتصر على نصيبه لكن يفسد به نصيب الآخر فيثبت له خيرة الاعتاق والتضمين والاستسعاء كما هو مذهبه فاذا اعتق لم يبق له خيار التضمين والاستسعاء واعتاقه يقتصر على نصيبه لانه يتجزى عنده ولكن يفسد به نصیب شريكه فله ان يضمنه قيمة نصيبه وله خيار العتق والاستسعاء ايضا كما هو مذهبه ويضمنه قيمة نصيبه مدبرا لان الاعتاق صادف المدبر
ترجمہ اگر ایک غلام دو شخصوں میں مشترک ہو جن میں سے ایک نے اس کو مد بر کیا۔ پھر دوسرے نے آزاد کر دیا اور حال یہ کہ وہ خوشحال ہے تو جس نے اس کو مد بر کیا ہے وہ چاہے معتق سے بحساب مدبر ہونے کے نصف قیمت کا تاوان لے چاہے غلام سے سعایت کرائے چاہے آزاد کر دے اور اگر ایک نے آزاد کیا پھر دوسرے نے مدبر کیا تو مد بر کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا کہ معتق سے تاوان لے بلکہ وہ غلام سے سعایت کرائے یا آزاد کرے۔ یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ تدبیر ان کے نزدیک متجری ہے تو ایک کامد بر کرنا اس کے حصہ تک رہے گا۔ لیکن اس سے دوسرے کا حصہ خراب ہو جائے گا۔ پس اس کو آزاد کرنے ، تاوان لینے اور سعایت کرانے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ امام صاحب کا مذہب ہے۔ پس جب اس نے آزاد کر دیا تو اس کو تاوان لینے اور سعایت کرانے کا اختیار نہیں رہا اور اس کا آزاد کر نا اسی کے حصہ تک رہا کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اعتماق مجری ہے لیکن اس سے اس کے شریک کا حصہ بگڑ جائے گا۔ اس لئے اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنے حصہ کی قیمت کا تاوان لے لے اور اس کو آزاد کرنے اور سعایت کرانے کا بھی اختیار ہے۔ جیسا کہ امام صاحب کا مذہب ہے اور اپنے حصہ کی قیمت کا تاوان مدبر ہونے کے حساب سے لے گا۔ کیونکہ آزاد کرنا ایک مدبر سے متصل ہوا ہے۔ تشریح قول وان كان العبد - الخ ۔ ایک غلام دو آدمیوں میں مشترک تھا ان میں سے ایک نے اپنا حصہ مدبر کر دیا اس کے بعد دوسرے نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا اور آزاد کننده مالدار ہے تو مد بر کرنے والے کو تین اختیار ہیں چاہے آزاد کنندہ سے مدبر کی نصف قیمت کا تاوان لے کیونکہ معتق کے آزاد کرنے سے اس کا حصہ فاسد ہو گیا۔ اور چاہے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دے اور چاہے غلام سے سعایت کر اور اگر شریکین میں سے ایک نے پہلے آزاد کیا پھر دوسرے نے مدبر کیا تو اب مدبر کو صرف دو چیزوں کا اختیار ہو گا چاہے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دے چاہے غلام سے سعایت کرالے۔ معتق سے تاوان نہیں لے سکتا۔ یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ آپ کے نزدیک تدبیر متجری ہے تو ایک شریک کا مدبر کرنا اسی کے حصہ تک رہے گا۔ مگر اس تدبیر سے چونکہ دوسرے کا حصہ خراب ہو گیا ( لسد باب النقل على الآخر ) اس لئے شریک ثانی کو مذہب امام کے بموجب مذکورہ خیارات ثلاثہ حاصل ہوں گے اور جب اس نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کر دیا تو اب اس کو تاوان وسعایت کا اختیار نہ ہوگا اور اس کا اعتاق اس کے حصہ تک رہے گا۔ کیونکہ اعتاق بھی ان کے نزدیک متجری ہے۔ لیکن اس اعتاق سے چونکہ دوسرے کا حصہ خراب ہو گیا ( سند باب الاستخدام علیہ ) اس لئے اس کو اختیار ہوگا کہ اپنے حصہ کی قیمت کا تاوان لے اور یہ بھی اختیار ہوگا کہ آزاد کرے یا غلام سے سعایت کرائے ۔ اب اگر وہ تاوان لیتا ہے تو تاوان مد بر ہونے کے حساب سے لیگا کیونکہ آزاد کرنا ایک مدبر سے متصل ہوا ہے۔
مد بر کی قیمت کیسے معلوم کی جائے گی
ثم قيل قيمة المدبر تعرف بتقويم المقومين وقيل يجب ثلثا قيمته وهو قن لان المنافع انواع ثلاثة البيع واشباهه والاستخدام و امثاله والاعتاق وتوابعه والفائت البيع فيسقط الثلث واذا ضمنه لا يتملكه بالضمان لانه لا يقبل الانتقال من ملك الى ملك كما اذا غصب مديرا فابق وان اعتقه احدهما اولا كان للآخر الخيارات الثلاث عنده فاذا دبره لم يبق له خيار التضمين وبقى خيار الاعتاق والاستسعاء لان المدبر يُعتق ويُستسعى وقال ابويوسف ومحمد اذا دبّره احدهما فعتق الآخر باطل لانه لا يتجزى عندهما فيتملك نصیب صاحبه بالتدبير ويضمن نصف قيمته موسرا كان او معسرا لانه ضمان تملك فلا يختلف باليسار والاعسار ويضمن نصف قيمته قنا لانه صادفه التدبير وهو قنّ وان اعتقه احدهما فتدبير الآخر باطل لان الاعتاق لا يتجزى فيعتق كله فلم يصادف التدبير الملك وهو يعقده ويضمن نصف قيمته ان كان موسرا العبد في ذلك ان كان معسرا لان هذا ضمان الاعتاق فيختلف ذلك باليسار والاعسار عندهما ويسعى
ترجمہ پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ مدبر کی قیمت دو اندازہ کنندہ گان کے انداہ کرنے سے معلوم ہو جائیگی۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ محض مملوک کی دو تہائی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ منافع تین قسم کے ہوتے ہیں بیع اور اس کے مانند، خدمت لینا اور اس کے مثل آزاد کرنا اور اس کے توابع ، اور یہاں صرف بیع کا فائدہ جاتا رہا تو ایک تہائی قیمت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور جب اس نے ضمان دے دیا تو وہ اس کا مالک نہ ہوگا کیونکہ مد بر ایک ملک سے دوسری ملک کی طرف منتقل ہونے کے لائق نہیں ہے جیسے کسی مدبر کو غصب کیا اور وہ بھاگ گیا اور اگر پہلے ایک شریک نے آزاد کیا تو دوسرے شریک کو تینوں اختیارات ہوں گے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک پھر جب دوسرے نے مدبر کر دیا تو اس کو تاوان لینے کا اختیار نہیں رہا۔ اور آزاد کرنے یا سعایت کرانے کا اختیار رہ گیا کیونکہ مدیر آزاد کیا جا سکتا ہے اور اس سے سعایت کرائی جاسکتی ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جب ایک نے مدبر کر دیا تو دوسرے کا آزاد کرنا باطل ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک مدبر کرنا متجزمی نہیں ہے تو وہ مد بر کرنے سے اپنے شریک کے حصہ کا مالک ہو گیا۔ اور اس کی نصف قیمت کا ضامن ہو گیا خوشحال ہو یا تنگدست کیونکہ یہ ضمان تملک ہے پس خوشحالی تنگدستی سے مختلف نہ ہوگا اور اس کی نصف قیمت کا تاوان محض مملوک ہونے کے حساب سے دے گا۔ کیونکہ مذبیر اس اس حال میں متصل ہوئی کہ وہ محض مملوک تھا اور اگر ایک نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو دوسرے کا مد بر کرنا باطل ہے۔ کیونکہ اعتاق متجری نہیں ہے تو وہ پورا آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ پس تدبیر ملک سے متصل نہ ہوئی حالانکہ تدبیر کا اعتماد ملک پر ہی ہے اور اسکی نصف قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا اگر خوشحال ہو اور غلام نصف قیمت میں سعایت کرے گا۔ اگر وہ تنگدست ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ ضمان اعتاق ہے تو یہ صاحبین کے نزدیک
Book of Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 12. A slave shared between two men, one made him mudabbar, the other freed him, and he is wealthy. The one who made him mudabbar may, if he wishes, hold the manumitter liable for half his value as a mudabbar, or if he wishes, have the slave earn money, or if he wishes, free him. If one freed him and the other made him mudabbar, then he cannot hold the manumitter liable, but may have the slave earn money or free him. He (Abu Hanifa) said: 'If the slave was between two men, one made him mudabbar, then the other freed him while he is wealthy, then if the one who made him mudabbar wishes, he may hold the manumitter liable for half his value as a mudabbar, or if he wishes, have the slave earn money, or if he wishes, free him. And if one freed him then the other made him mudabbar, he does not have the option to hold the manumitter liable, but may have the slave earn money or free him. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The reason is that tadbir is divisible according to him, so the tadbir of one is confined to his share, but it spoils the other's share, so he has the options of freeing, claiming compensation, and seeking earnings as per his madhhab. When he freed, he no longer has the option of compensation and seeking earnings, and his freeing is confined to his share because it is divisible according to him, but it spoils his partner's share, so he may claim compensation for the value of his share, and he also has the option of freeing and seeking earnings as per his madhhab, and he claims compensation for his share as a mudabbar because the freeing encountered the mudabbar.' Translation: If a slave is shared between two persons, one of whom made him mudabbar, then the other freed him while he is wealthy, then the one who made him mudabbar may, if he wishes, take compensation from the manumitter for half the value as mudabbar, or if he wishes, have the slave earn, or if he wishes, free him. And if one freed him then the other made him mudabbar, then the one who made him mudabbar does not have the option to take compensation from the manumitter, but may have the slave earn or free him. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and its reason is that tadbir is divisible according to him, so one's making mudabbar remains confined to his share, but it spoils the other's share. So he has the options of freeing, taking compensation, and seeking earnings as per Imam's madhhab. Then when he frees, he no longer has the option of compensation and seeking earnings, and his freeing remains confined to his share because it is divisible according to Imam, but it spoils his partner's share. Therefore, he has the option to take compensation for his share's value, and he also has the option to free or have the slave earn. As per Imam's madhhab, he will take compensation for his share as a mudabbar because the freeing encountered a mudabbar. Explanation of the statement 'And if the slave was...' : A slave was shared between two men, one of them made his share mudabbar, then the other freed his share while the freedman is wealthy. Then the one who made mudabbar has three options: either take compensation from the freedman for half the mudabbar's value because the manumitter's freeing spoiled his share, or free his share, or have the slave earn. If one of the partners freed first then the other made mudabbar, then the mudabbar now only has two options: either free his share or have the slave earn. He cannot take compensation from the manumitter. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the reason is that according to him tadbir is divisible, so one partner's making mudabbar remains confined to his share, but since this tadbir spoiled the other partner's share, the second partner according to Imam's madhhab obtains the three options mentioned. And when he freed his share, he no longer has the option of compensation and seeking earnings, and his freeing remains confined to his share because it is also divisible according to him, but since this freeing spoiled the other's share, he has the option to take compensation for his share's value, and he also has the option to free or have the slave earn. If he takes compensation, he will take it as a mudabbar because the freeing encountered a mudabbar. How is the value of a mudabbar determined? Then it was said: The value of the mudabbar is known by the valuation of the assessors. And it was said: Two-thirds of his value as a mere slave is obligatory because benefits are of three types: sale and similar, utilization and similar, freeing and its dependencies. The benefit of sale is lost, so one-third is dropped. And when he gives compensation, he does not become owner by it because it does not accept transfer from one ownership to another, like if someone wrongfully took a mudabbar and he ran away. And if one freed him first, the other has the three options according to him (Abu Hanifa). When he made him mudabbar, he no longer has the option of compensation, and the options of freeing and seeking earnings remain because the mudabbar can be freed and can be made to earn. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: When one makes him mudabbar, the freeing by the other is void because tadbir is not divisible according to them. So he becomes owner of his partner's share by the tadbir and guarantees half his value, whether he is wealthy or poor, because it is a guarantee of ownership, so it does not differ by wealth or poverty. He guarantees half his value as a mere slave because the tadbir encountered him while he was a mere slave. And if one freed him, then the tadbir of the other is void because freeing is not divisible, so he becomes entirely free. Thus, tadbir did not encounter ownership, and he (the one who made tadbir) guarantees half his value if he is wealthy, and the slave has to earn half his value if he is poor, because this is a guarantee of freeing, so it differs by wealth and poverty according to them. Translation: Then it was said that the value of a mudabbar is known by the estimation of two assessors. And it was said that two-thirds of his value as a mere slave is obligatory because benefits are of three types: sale and its like, service and its like, freeing and its dependencies. Here only the benefit of sale is lost, so one-third of the value is dropped. And when he gave compensation, he does not become its owner because a mudabbar is not fit for transfer from one ownership to another, like a mudabbar that was wrongfully taken and ran away. And if one partner freed first, the other partner has the three options according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Then when the other made him mudabbar, he no longer has the option of taking compensation, and the options of freeing and seeking earnings remain because a mudabbar can be freed and can be made to earn. The two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: When one makes him mudabbar, the freeing by the other is void because tadbir is not divisible according to them. So he becomes owner of his partner's share by the tadbir and guarantees half its value, whether wealthy or poor, because this is a guarantee of ownership, so it does not differ by wealth or poverty. And he guarantees half its value as a mere slave because the tadbir encountered him while he was a mere slave. And if one freed him, then the tadbir of the other is void because freeing is not divisible, so he becomes entirely free. Thus, tadbir did not encounter ownership, and he guarantees half its value if the freedman is wealthy, and the slave has to earn half its value if he is poor, because this is a guarantee of freeing, so it differs by wealth and poverty according to them.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute from Kitab al-Mukatab, focusing on a shared slave where one partner makes him mudabbar and the other frees him. The core issue is whether tadbir (promise of freedom after death) and itq (immediate freeing) are divisible (tajazzi) in a jointly owned slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that both tadbir and itq are divisible, meaning each partner's action applies only to his own share but affects the other's share. Therefore, if one makes the slave mudabbar and the other frees him (when wealthy), the mudabbar partner has three options: claim compensation from the manumitter for half the mudabbar's value, free his own share, or have the slave earn his share. If the order is reversed (first free, then mudabbar), the mudabbar partner only has two options (free his share or have the slave earn) because the freeing already happened, eliminating the compensation option. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they consider tadbir and itq indivisible (la yatajazza). Thus, if one makes mudabbar, he automatically owns the other's share and must pay half the slave's value as a mere slave (not mudabbar) regardless of the manumitter's wealth. If one frees first, the slave is entirely free, so later tadbir is void, and the second partner guarantees half the value only if the manumitter is wealthy (otherwise the slave earns it). The passage also discusses how to value a mudabbar for compensation: either by expert valuation or as two-thirds of the slave's value (since one-third of the benefits—sale—are lost due to the mudabbar status). Imam Abu Hanifa's position gives the mudabbar partner more flexibility, while the Sahibayn's view provides more certainty and protects the freed slave from being re-enslaved. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it is the majority opinion and more commonly adopted.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whom his master has promised freedom after the master's death, effective upon the master's death if the slave is still alive.
تدبير (tadbir): The act of making a slave mudabbar; a promise of freedom after the owner's death, which is a binding contract but does not immediately free the slave.
تضمين (tadmin): Holding someone liable for compensation; in this context, the option of the mudabbar partner to claim half the value from the manumitter.
استسعاء (istis'ā'): Requiring the slave to earn money to pay for his freedom; the slave is made to work and pay his value in installments.
تجزئ (tajazzi'): Divisibility; the quality of a legal act (like tadbir or itq) that can be applied to a part of a thing (like a share of a slave).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a jointly owned slave is made mudabbar by one partner and then freed by the other partner (who is wealthy), what options does the first partner have?
A) Only to free his own share.
B) To claim compensation from the manumitter, free his share, or have the slave earn.
C) To force the manumitter to pay the full value of the slave.
D) The mudabbar is void, and the slave is free.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of tadbir and itq determines whether a co-owner whose share is affected has options (compensation, freeing, or earning) or faces forced transfer or voidance; the Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's view of divisibility.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Divisibility of Tadbir
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tadbir divisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the divisibility of tadbir and identify the practical consequences when one co-owner frees a share and the other makes a tadbir.

Core Idea
Tadbir is divisible according to Abu Hanifa, not Sahibayn — the first act dominates.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding a jointly-owned slave when one owner frees his share and the other declares tadbir. The ruling hinges on whether tadbir is divisible (yatajazza) like partial emancipation or indivisible. We will explore the different conclusions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two sequences: (1) one co-owner frees his share first, then the other makes tadbir; (2) one co-owner makes tadbir first, then the other tries to free. Determine which scenario is being analyzed for each position.
The text first addresses scenario 1 under Abu Hanifa's view, then scenario 2 under Sahibayn's view.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position on tadbir divisibility
According to Abu Hanifa, tadbir is divisible (yatajazza). Therefore, after one co-owner frees his share, the other can still make a valid tadbir on his own share. The second co-owner loses the option of demanding compensation (daman) but retains the options of freeing his share or making the slave earn (istis'a').
The reasoning involves the valuation of a mudabbir: only one-third of the value is lost because only the benefit of sale is lost.
3
Outline the three options after first itq
When one co-owner frees his share, the other co-owner has three options according to Abu Hanifa: (a) free his own share, (b) demand compensation from the first co-owner, or (c) make the slave work (istis'a'). If he then makes tadbir, option (b) is removed.
Tadbir restricts the ability to transfer ownership, so compensation is no longer possible.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, tadbir is indivisible (la yatajazza), similar to emancipation. Thus, if one co-owner makes tadbir first, the other cannot free; the one who made tadbir owns the other's share and pays half the value as daman tamalluk (invariable). If one frees first, the subsequent tadbir is invalid because the slave is fully free.
The difference in daman types: daman tamalluk is not means-tested; daman itq is means-tested.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the second co-owner can still make a valid tadbir after the first frees, and the slave remains partially enslaved until the second acts. Under the Sahibayn, the first act (itq or tadbir) dominates, and the other's act is void. The compensation rules also differ.
Both positions are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah; Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قيل قيمة المدبر تعرف بتقويم المقومين وقيل يجب ثلثا قيمته وهو قن لان المنافع انواع ثلاثة البيع واشباهه والاستخدام و امثاله والاعتاق وتوابعه والفائت البيع فيسقط الثلث واذا ضمنه لا يتملكه بالضمان لانه لا يقبل الانتقال من ملك الى ملك كما اذا غصب مديرا فابق وان اعتقه احدهما اولا كان للآخر الخيارات الثلاث عنده فاذا دبره لم يبق له خيار التضمين وبقى خيار الاعتاق والاستسعاء لان المدبر يُعتق ويُستسعى وقال ابويوسف ومحمد اذا دبّره احدهما فعتق الآخر باطل لانه لا يتجزى عندهما فيتملك نصیب صاحبه بالتدبير ويضمن نصف قيمته موسرا كان او معسرا لانه ضمان تملك فلا يختلف باليسار والاعسار ويضمن نصف قيمته قنا لانه صادفه التدبير وهو قنّ وان اعتقه احدهما فتدبير الآخر باطل لان الاعتاق لا يتجزى فيعتق كله فلم يصادف التدبير الملك وهو يعقده ويضمن نصف قيمته ان كان موسرا العبد في ذلك ان كان معسرا لان هذا ضمان الاعتاق فيختلف ذلك باليسار والاعسار عندهما ويسعى
Then it was said: the value of the mudabbir is known by the valuation of the valuators. And it was said: two-thirds of his value is obligatory, and he is a qinn (full slave). Because the benefits (manafi') are of three types: sale and its likes, utilization (istikhdam) and its likes, and emancipation (itq) and its consequences. The loss here is only the benefit of sale, so one-third is dropped. And if he guarantees (the slave) by compensation, he does not become its owner by the guarantee because it does not accept transfer from one ownership to another, just as if someone wrongfully seizes a mudabbir and he escapes. And if one of them (the co-owners) frees (his share) first, then the other has three options according to him (Abu Hanifa). So when he makes him a mudabbir, he no longer has the option of demanding compensation, and the options of emancipation and istis'a' (making the slave earn his freedom) remain. Because the mudabbir can be freed and can be made to earn. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If one of them makes him a mudabbir, the other's emancipation is invalid, because according to them (tadbir) is not divisible. So he (the one who made tadbir) owns his partner's share by the tadbir, and he guarantees half his value, whether he is wealthy or poor, because it is a guarantee of ownership, so it does not vary with wealth and poverty. And he guarantees half his value as a qinn (full slave), because the tadbir found him while he was a qinn. And if one of them frees him, then the tadbir of the other is invalid, because emancipation is not divisible, so he becomes fully free. So the tadbir did not encounter ownership, and (the one who freed) guarantees half his value if he is wealthy; the slave works for that if he is poor, because this is a guarantee of emancipation, so it varies with wealth and poverty according to them. And he (the slave) works (to earn).
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a slave owned jointly by two persons. It addresses the scenarios where one co-owner acts (by freeing or making tadbir) and the subsequent rights of the other co-owner. The passage begins by explaining how to value a mudabbir slave for compensation purposes. Two opinions are mentioned: the first is that the value is determined by expert appraisers; the second is that only two-thirds of the full slave's value is taken into account. The reasoning is that a slave's utility (manafi') falls into three categories: (1) the right to sell and transfer ownership, (2) the right to use and hire out, and (3) the right to emancipate and its consequences (like kitaba, tadbir, etc.). In a mudabbir, only the first category (sale) is lost, since a mudabbir cannot be sold. Therefore one-third of the value is dropped, and two-thirds remains as the basis for compensation. The passage then explains that if one co-owner emancipates his share first, the other co-owner acquires three options according to Imam Abu Hanifa: he may free his own share, demand compensation from the first co-owner, or make the slave work for his freedom (istis'a'). However, if the second co-owner then makes the slave a mudabbir (promises freedom upon his death), the option of demanding compensation is lost because a mudabbir cannot be transferred by sale or compensation. The remaining options of freeing and istis'a' are still available. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad disagree with this analysis. According to them, tadbir (like emancipation) is non-divisible (la yatajazza). Therefore, if one co-owner makes the slave a mudabbir, it affects the entire slave, and the other co-owner cannot subsequently emancipate his share—any such emancipation is invalid. Instead, the one who made the tadbir acquires ownership of the other's share through the tadbir, and is obligated to pay half the slave's value as compensation, regardless of whether he is wealthy or poor, because this is a guarantee of ownership (daman tamalluk) which does not depend on financial status. The valuation is based on the slave's full value as a qinn (unrestricted slave), since the tadbir took effect while the slave was still a full slave. Conversely, if one co-owner emancipates first, the other's subsequent tadbir is invalid according to the Sahibayn. The emancipation is absolute and indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free. The tadbir does not take effect because there is no remaining ownership. The co-owner who freed must pay half the value as compensation if he is wealthy; if he is poor, the slave must work to earn that amount (istis'a'). This is a guarantee of emancipation (daman itq), which varies with wealth and poverty. The practical difference (thamara al-khilaf) is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, tadbir is divisible, so a co-owner can make a valid tadbir regarding his share alone, and the other co-owner retains the option to emancipate or seek compensation. According to the Sahibayn, tadbir is indivisible, so the first act (whether itq or tadbir) prevails and the other's act is invalid, and the compensation rules differ accordingly.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A master's declaration that a slave will become free after the master's death, making the slave a mudabbir.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the owner's death; such a slave cannot be sold or transferred.
ضمان تملک (daman tamalluk): A guarantee of ownership, a compensation that makes the person become owner; this does not vary with wealth/poverty.
ضمان اعتاق (daman itq): A guarantee of emancipation, compensation paid when one person's emancipation affects another's rights; varies with wealth/poverty.
استسعاء (istis'a'): Making the slave work to earn his freedom or to pay a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one co-owner frees his share of a slave and the other co-owner then makes the slave a mudabbir, what options does the second co-owner have?
A) He may free his own share or demand compensation from the first co-owner.
B) He may free his own share or make the slave work (istis'a'), but not demand compensation.
C) He may demand compensation or make the slave work, but not free his own share.
D) He loses all options and must accept whatever the first co-owner did.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of tadbir is a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows partial tadbir, Sahibayn do not, leading to different rules for co-ownership scenarios.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Mudabbar Freed by One Co-Owner
Intra-Hanafi dispute on co-owner's options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a mudabbar freed by one co-owner and state the practical options for the second co-owner.

Core Idea
Tadbir and itaq are divisible per Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn say indivisible — outcomes differ.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when one co-owner frees his share of a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom at the master's death), what rights does the other co-owner retain? Imam Abu Hanifa provides three options, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) restrict them. The underlying cause is whether tadbir and itaq are divisible acts. The passage also explains the valuation of a mudabbar based on the three types of benefit.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the case: two co-owners of a mudabbar slave; one frees his share. What are the options for the other?
The scenario is from the matn: 'and if one of them frees him...'
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the second co-owner has three options: free his own share, claim half the mudabbar's value from the first co-owner (if wealthy), or seek sa'aya from the slave.
Tadbir is divisible, so the second co-owner's rights remain intact.
3
Identify Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that tadbir is indivisible; the first co-owner becomes full owner of the mudabbar and owes half the value of a pure slave to the second, regardless of wealth. If the first freed before the second made it mudabbar, the freeing is void.
They also hold itaq is indivisible, so if the first freed first, the whole slave is free.
4
Understand the valuation
The mudabbar's value is two-thirds of a pure slave because three benefits (sale, use, liberation) exist; tadbir removes sale, losing one-third of value.
This qiyas is based on the illa of loss of one benefit type.
5
Apply the thamarah
Under Abu Hanifa, the second co-owner has three real choices; under Sahibayn, his options are limited (cannot free his share if tadbir occurred first; can only claim value or sa'aya if freeing occurred first).
The practical difference is whether the second co-owner can free his share.

صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جب شریکین میں سے ایک نے مدبر کر دیا تو دوسرے کا آزاد کرنا باطل ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں تدبیر متجری نہیں ہے۔ پس وہ مدبر کرنے سے اپنے شریک کے حصہ کا مالک ہو گیا اور اس کی نصف قیمت کا ضامن خوشحال ہو یا تنگدست کیونکہ ضمان تملک ہے تو یسار و اعسار سے مختلف نہ ہوگا اور نصف قیمت عبد محض کے حساب سے دے گا کیونکہ تدبیر ایسی حالت میں ہوئی کہ وہ محض مملوک تھا۔ قوله وان اعتقه احدهما .... الخ - Commentary on his statement 'then before...' - In the ruling of the discussed issue it was stated that after one partner frees [a mudabbar], the one who made [the slave] mudabbar will have three options, one of which is: if he wishes, he can take half the value of the mudabbar from the one who freed [his share]. Now how will the value of the mudabbar be assessed? There are different opinions about this. Some said that the value of the mudabbar is determined by appraisers. And some said that two-thirds of the value of a pure slave will be obligatory. Because the benefits are of three types: (1) Sale and similar matters that result in the removal of ownership, like gift, charity, inheritance, bequest - just as sale removes ownership of the corpus, these also remove it. (2) Utilization, i.e., taking service, or matters similar to utilization in deriving benefit, like hire, lending, guardianship. (3) Liberation without compensation (i'tinaq) and its correlates, like kitaba, istilad, tadbir, and freeing for compensation. For in these matters, the outcome is freedom. Now in making mudabbar, only the first type, i.e., the benefit of sale, is lost because he can no longer sell him. Therefore one-third of the value falls away, and two-thirds remain obligatory. In any case, when the manumitter pays the compensation for the mudabbar, he does not become the owner of the mudabbar's share because the mudabbar is not capable of being transferred from one ownership to another. For example, if someone usurped a mudabbar and he ran away, the usurper is liable for compensation in the same measure even though he does not become its owner. Thus this indemnity is not for ownership but is an indemnity for interposing between the owner and the owned, because through this i'tinaq he eliminated the master's right of utilization etc., so he becomes like a usurper. His statement: 'And if one of them frees him...' - This is a statement of the second part of the book: if one of the co-owners freed [the slave] first, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the other co-owner has the three aforementioned options (itaq, tadmeen, and sa'aya). Because although the manumitter confined himself to his own share, he ruined the share of the other co-owner. Then when the second co-owner made him mudabbar, the mudabbar will have only two options: either free his share or seek payment from the slave (sa'aya). He cannot take compensation from the manumitter because it is possible to free the mudabbar or seek payment from him. His statement: 'And Abu Yusuf said...' - The Sahibayn say: when one of the co-owners makes [the slave] mudabbar, the freeing by the other is void. Because according to them, tadbir is not divisible. So by making mudabbar, he became owner of his partner's share and is guarantor of half its value whether wealthy or poor, because the indemnity is for ownership (daman tamalluk), so it does not differ based on wealth, and he will pay half the value of a pure slave because at the time of tadbir he was a pure slave. His statement: 'And if one of them frees him...' - Also, if one frees first and then the other makes him mudabbar, it is void because according to them, freeing is also indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free, then the tadbir is not connected to ownership. Yet validity of tadbir requires ownership to exist. Now the manumitter will be guarantor of half its value, provided he is wealthy; otherwise the slave will perform sa'aya. Because this is a daman i'tinaq, which according to the Sahibayn differs based on wealth.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a mudabbar slave shared between two owners. The commentator first discusses the valuation of a mudabbar: some say it is assessed by appraisers, but the preferred view is that it is two-thirds of the value of a pure slave because the mudabbar retains two of the three types of benefit (utilization and potential freedom) but loses the benefit of sale. This valuation applies to the calculation of indemnity. The core dispute: When one co-owner frees his share of a mudabbar, what are the options of the other co-owner? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the second co-owner has three options: (1) free his own share, (2) claim half the value from the first co-owner (if wealthy), or (3) seek payment from the slave (sa'aya). According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), tadbir is indivisible, so the one who made the slave mudabbar becomes full owner and owes half the value of a pure slave to the first co-owner, regardless of wealth. If the first co-owner frees his share before the other makes it mudabbar, then the freeing is effective and the second co-owner's tadbir is void because freeing is also indivisible. In that case, the first co-owner must pay half value only if wealthy; otherwise the slave performs sa'aya. The difference between the two views is rooted in whether tadbir and itaq are divisible (Imam Abu Hanifa) or not (Sahibayn). The commentator follows the order of the matn, first stating the ruling, then explaining the valuation, then presenting the two positions.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death.
اعتاق (itaq): Emancipation of a slave.
تضمین (tadmeen): Indemnity; payment of the value of the slave's share.
سعایت (sa'aya): The slave's effort to earn and pay for his freedom.
بیع (bay'): Sale; one of the three types of benefit in a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what options does the second co-owner have when the first co-owner frees his share of a mudabbar?
A) Only one option: to free his own share.
B) Three options: free his share, claim half value from the first co-owner, or seek payment from the slave.
C) Two options: claim full value or free the slave.
D) No options because the tadbir is void.

Key Takeaway
The division of tadbir and itaq among co-owners is a contested issue within the Hanafi school, with direct practical consequences for the second co-owner's options.

The Judge's Waiting Period for a Mukatib in Default
Ruling with proof on judge's waiting period for a defaulting mukatib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the judge's waiting period when a mukatib defaults on an installment and apply the derived proof from the story of Musa and Khidr.

Core Idea
A defaulting mukatib gets two to three days' grace before the judge annuls the kitaba.

When a mukatib (a slave under a kitaba contract to earn his freedom) fails to pay an installment, the judge must not rush to annul the contract. Instead, he investigates whether the mukatib has any incoming funds. If there is hope, the judge waits two or three days — a period derived from the three-strike pattern in the Quranic story of Musa and Khidr. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The judge must first check if the mukatib has a debt receivable or expected property. If so, do not declare inability immediately; wait two or three days.
This is a judicial procedure, not an automatic default.
2
Understand the purpose of the waiting period
The waiting period balances the interests of both master and mukatib, giving the mukatib a chance to pay.
Hanafi fiqh emphasizes 'consideration for both sides' (nazar li al-janibayn).
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The three-day period is based on the story of Musa and Khidr: after three incidents, Khidr said 'This is a parting between me and you' (Quran 18:78). By analogy, the judge gives three days as the maximum patience limit.
This is a qiyas on the established three-day periods for defense, debt payment, and khiyar.
4
Apply the ruling to the case when the mukatib has no means
If after waiting there is no hope and the master requests it, the judge declares the mukatib unable (ta'jiz) and annuls the kitaba.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, possibly differing from Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
