Mukatab Dies Leaving a Purchased Child: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the inclusion of a purchased child in the kitabah contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the purchased child's obligation upon the mukatab's death, identify the key distinction, and explain the inheritance consequence if the child is a son.

Core Idea
A purchased child is not automatically included in the father's kitabah contract, so he must pay immediately or be enslaved (Abu Hanifa), unlike a child born during kitabah.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The case involves a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) who dies leaving a child he purchased during the kitabah period. The key question: does the purchased child inherit the benefit of paying the kitabah in installments, or must he pay immediately? The passage also addresses a special case: if the mukatab purchased his own son, the son inherits from him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the purchased child upon the mukatab's death. Abu Hanifa says the child must pay immediately or be enslaved; the Sahibayn say the child can pay in installments.
2
Analyze the opposing proof
Understand the Sahibayn's analogy (qiyas) with a child born during kitabah. They argue that both are dependents (tabi'), so the purchased child should also have deferment.
The 'jami' (common point) is that the child is a dependent and the master can emancipate him.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on the time of connection to the contract. The term (ajal) is a condition of the contract and applies only to those who entered the contract. The purchased child was separate at the time of the contract, so the ruling does not extend to him.
The child born during kitabah was connected (mutassil) at the time of the contract, so the ruling extends.
4
Apply the distinction to the inheritance scenario
If the purchased child is the father's own son (i.e., the mukatab bought his son), then the son inherits from the father because both are deemed free at the father's death due to the dependency (taba'iyyah). This is separate from the dispute above.
The inheritance ruling applies only when the purchased child is the father's biological son.

Source Text

وان ترک ولدا مشترى فى الكتابة قيل له اما ان تودي بدل الكتابة حالة او ترد رقيقا عند ابي حنيفة واما عندهما يؤديه الى اجله اعتبارا بالولد المولود في الكتابة والجامع انه مكاتب عليه تبعا له ولهذا يملك المولى اعتاقه بخلاف سائر اکسابه ولابي حنيفة وهو الفرق بين الفصلين ان الاجل يثبت شرطا في العقد فيثبت في حق من دخل تحت العقد والمشترى لم يدخل لانه لم يُضَف اليه العقد ولا سرى حكمه اليه لانفصاله بخلاف المولود فى الكتابة لانه متصل وقت الكتابة فسرى الحكم اليه وحيث دخل في حكمه سعى فى نجومه فان اشترى ابنه ثم مات وترك وقاء ورثه ابنه لانه لما حكم بحريته في آخر جزء من اجزاء حياته يحكم بحرية ابنه في ذلك الوقت لانه تبع لابيه فى الكتابة فيكون هذا حرا يرث عن حر و كذلك ان كان هو وابنه مكاتبين كتابةً واحدةً لان الولد ان كان صغيراً فهو تبع لابيه وان كان كبيرا جعلا كشخص واحد فاذا حكم بحرية الاب يحكم بحريته في تلك الحالة على مامر
ترجمہ اگر چھوڑا کتابت میں خریدا ہوا فرزند تو اس سے کہا جائے گا کہ یا تو ادا کر بدل کتابت فی الحال یا کر دیا جائے گا رقیق ۔ امام ابو
If he left a child purchased during the kitabah, then he will be told: either pay the kitabah payment immediately or be returned to slavery according to Abu Hanifa. But according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he pays it by its term, in consideration of the child born during kitabah. And the common point is that he is a mukatab on him as a dependent, and for this reason the master has the right to emancipate him, unlike other earnings. And for Abu Hanifa, the difference between the two cases is that the term is established as a condition in the contract, so it is established for those who enter under the contract. The purchased child did not enter because the contract was not attributed to him, nor did its ruling extend to him due to his separateness, unlike the child born during kitabah because he was connected at the time of the kitabah, so the ruling extended to him. And when he entered under its ruling, he works for its installments. Then if he bought his son, then died, and left wealth, his son inherits from him because when freedom is judged for him in the last part of his life, his son's freedom is also judged at that time because he is dependent (tabi') on his father in the kitabah, so this one becomes free, inheriting from a free person. And similarly if he and his son were both mukatabs in a single kitabah contract; because if the child is minor, he is dependent on his father, and if he is adult, they are considered as one person. So when freedom is judged for the father, freedom is also judged for him in that state as previously mentioned. Translation: If he left a child purchased during the kitabah, he will be told: either pay the kitabah payment immediately or be made a slave. Imam Abu...
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The matn addresses the case where a mukatab dies leaving a child he purchased (i.e., a child who was already a slave and was bought by the mukatab during the kitabah period). According to Abu Hanifa, such a purchased child is not automatically included in the father's kitabah contract because the child was separate at the time of the contract. Therefore, the child must either pay the remaining kitabah amount immediately (as a lump sum) or be returned to slavery. In contrast, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) analogize to the child born during kitabah, holding that the purchased child should also have the deferment (ajal) of the installments because he is a dependent (tabi') of the father in the kitabah. The text then provides the reasoning for Abu Hanifa's position: the term (ajal) is a condition in the contract and applies only to those who entered the contract originally; the purchased child did not enter because the contract was not attributed to him, and its ruling did not extend to him because he was separate (munfasil) at the time of the contract. The commentary then discusses inheritance: if the mukatab later buys his own son (who was already born and then purchased), and then dies leaving wealth, the son inherits from him because both are deemed free at the last part of the father's life. Similarly, if father and son are both mukatabs under a single contract, they are treated as one person, so the son's freedom follows the father's.

Key Terms
ولد مشترى (walad mushtara): A child purchased by the mukatab during the kitabah period, i.e., a slave child who was not born during the kitabah but acquired afterwards.
تابع (tabi'): A dependent; the child is dependent on the father in the kitabah contract, meaning his status follows the father's.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens if a mukatab dies leaving a purchased child and no other property?
A) The child must work to pay the kitabah in installments like a child born during kitabah
B) The child must pay the entire remaining kitabah amount immediately or be enslaved
C) The child automatically becomes free like the father
D) The child is not affected and remains free

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal difference on whether a purchased child inherits the deferment benefit; the key is the child's connection to the original kitabah contract.
